§ 10.01 TITLE OF CODE.
   All ordinances of a permanent and general nature, as revised, codified,
rearranged, renumbered and consolidated into component codes, titles, chapters
and sections, shall be known and designated as the "Town of Keystone Code," for
which designation "Code of Ordinances" or "Codified Ordinances" may be
substituted. Code title, chapter and section headings do not constitute any
part of the law as contained in the code.
§ 10.02 RULES OF INTERPRETATION.
   (A)   Generally. Unless otherwise provided herein, or by law or implication
required, the same rules of construction, definition and application shall
govern the interpretation of this code as those governing the interpretation of
state law.
   (B)   Specific rules of interpretation. The construction of all ordinances
shall be by the following rules, unless that construction is plainly repugnant
to the intent of the legislative body or of the context of the same ordinance.
      (1)   Acts by assistants. When a statute, code provision or ordinance
requires an act to be done which, by law, an agent or deputy as well may do as
the principal, that requisition shall be satisfied by the performance of the
act by an authorized agent or deputy.
      (2)   Gender; singular and plural; tenses. Words denoting the masculine
gender shall be deemed to include the feminine and neuter genders; words in the
singular shall include the plural, and words in the plural shall include the
singular; the use of a verb in the present tense shall include the future, if
applicable.
      (3)   General term. A general term following specific enumeration of
terms is not to be limited to the class enumerated unless expressly so limited.
General terms descriptive of an officer, act, proceeding or thing shall have
reference to a municipality concerned or affected.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
§ 10.03 CAPTIONS.
   Headings and captions used in this code other than the title, chapter and
section numbers are employed for reference purposes only and shall be not be
deemed a part of the text of any section.
§ 10.04 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this code of ordinances, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AND, OR.  OR may be read AND, and AND may be read OR, if the sense requires
it.
   BOARD. The Board of Trustees of the Town of Keystone, constituting the
governing body of the town.
   CODE. The ordinances of Keystone in their entirety, including each and every
section thereof. The entire code is intended by the Board of Trustees to
constitute an ordinance in revision of the ordinance of the town, within the
meaning of SDCL §§ 9-19-16 and 9-19-17.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   COMPUTATION OF TIME. The time in which any act provided by this code or
other ordinance is to be done is computed by excluding the first day and
including the last, unless the last is a holiday and then it also is excluded.
Fractions of a day are to be disregarded in computations which include more
than 1 day, and involve no questions of priority.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   COUNTY. Pennington County, South Dakota.
   DUTIES PERFORMED BY AGENTS. Wherever in this code any act is required to be
done by an officer in the line of his or her general duties, or by a department
head or inspector, the same shall be construed to permit the doing of the act
by the agent or subordinate of the person; provided that the agent or
subordinate is duly authorized and duly qualified to perform the act is not
otherwise required to be performed personally by the person, either by specific
law or by the nature of the act.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   ELECTOR(S) or QUALIFIED ELECTOR(S). Voter(s).
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   GENDER. A word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be
applied to females and to firms, partnerships, associations and corporations,
as well as to males.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   GENERALLY. The provisions of this code shall be liberally construed to
effect the purpose expressed therein or implied from the expression thereof. In
case of doubt or ambiguity in the meaning of the provisions, the general shall
yield to the particular. Reference for interpretation and construction shall
tend to further the accomplishment of the elimination of the particular
mischiefs for which the provisions were enacted. Words shall be construed in
their common and usual significance unless the contrary is clearly indicated.
   GOVERNING BODY. The Board of Trustees of the Town of Keystone, South Dakota.
   JOINT AUTHORITY. Words purporting to give authority to 2 or more officers or
other persons shall be construed as giving the authority to a majority of the
officers or other persons, unless it is otherwise declared.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   LOT. Includes PARCEL or TRACT OF LAND.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   MONTH. A calendar month.
   MUNICIPALITY or MUNICIPAL CORPORATION. All cities and towns organized under
the laws of this state but shall not include any other political subdivisions.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   OATH. Includes an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation
may be substituted for an oath, and in those cases the words SWEAR and SWORN
shall be equivalent to the words AFFIRM and AFFIRMED.
   OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES. Whenever reference is made in this code to a town
officer or employee by title only, this shall be construed as though followed
by the words "of the Town of Keystone" and shall be taken to mean the officer
or employee of the town having the title mentioned or performing the duties
indicated.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   ORDINANCE. A permanent legislative act within the limits of its powers of
the governing body of a municipality.
(SDCL § 9-19-1)
   OWNER. As used in this code relating to local improvements, the grantee in
the last deed of conveyance of any lot or parcel of land recorded in the office
of the register of deeds of the county or counties in which the municipality is
located, or his or her heirs or successors.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   PERSON. Associations, corporations, firms, partnerships and bodies politic
and corporate as well as to individuals.
   PUBLIC PLACE. Streets, alleys and sidewalks dedicated to public use, and
shall also include, but not be limited to, parts of buildings, schools,
athletic facilities and other premises, whether publicly-or privately-owned,
which are used by the general public or to which the general public is invited
commercially, for a fee, or otherwise, or in or on which the general public is
permitted without specific invitation.
   PUBLICATION. Any requirement for publication shall mean publication in the
official newspaper of the municipality concerned or affected, if any; but if
none, then in a legal newspaper published in the municipality, if any; but if
none, then in any legal newspaper which serves the municipality, except as
provided by SDCL § 9-13-13. Personal service either within or without the state
upon the person affected thereby by delivery of a copy of a notice required to
be published shall be equivalent to the required publication.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   RESOLUTION. Any determination that, decision, or direction of the governing
body of a municipality of a temporary or special character for the purpose of
initiating, effecting or carrying out its administrative duties and functions.
(SDCL § 9-19-1)
   SDCL. South Dakota Codified Laws.
   SIGNATURE or SUBSCRIPTION. A mark when a person cannot write.
   STATE. The State of South Dakota.
   STREET.  STREET includes AVENUE.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   TENSE. Words used in the past or present tense include the future as well as
the past and present.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   TOWN. The Town of Keystone, in the County of Pennington, and the State of
South Dakota.
   VARIATIONS IN PUNCTUATION AND TYPOGRAPHICAL ERRORS. No variation in
punctuation, either formal or informal, consistent or not, shall affect the
validity of this code, nor shall obvious or apparent defects in spelling or
typography be construed as to invalidate any portion hereof, so long as the
purpose and intent of the section is clear.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
   WRITTEN or IN WRITING. Any representation of words, letters or figures,
whether by printing or otherwise.
   YEAR. A calendar year.
§ 10.05 SEVERABILITY.
   If any provision of this code as now or later amended or its application to
any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect
other provisions that can be given effect without the invalid provision or
application.
§ 10.06 REFERENCE TO OTHER SECTIONS.
   Whenever in 1 section reference is made to another section hereof, that
reference shall extend and apply to the section referred to as subsequently
amended, revised, recodified or renumbered unless the subject matter is changed
or materially altered by the amendment or revision.
§ 10.07 REFERENCES TO OFFICES.
   Reference to a public office or officer shall be deemed to apply to any
office, officer or employee of this local government exercising the powers,
duties or functions contemplated in the provision, irrespective of any transfer
of functions or change in the official title of the functionary.
§ 10.08 ERRORS AND OMISSIONS.
   If a manifest error is discovered, consisting of the misspelling of any
words; the omission of any word or words necessary to express the intention of
the provisions affected; the use of a word or words to which no meaning can be
attached; or the use of a word or words when another word or words was clearly
intended to express the intent, the spelling shall be corrected and the word or
words supplied, omitted or substituted as will conform with the manifest
intention, and the provisions shall have the same effect as though the correct
words were contained in the text as originally published. No alteration shall
be made or permitted if any question exists regarding the nature or extent of
the error.
§ 10.09 POWERS TO ENACT, AMEND OR REPEAL ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS; GENERALLY.
   Every municipality may enact, make, amend, revise or repeal all such
ordinances, resolutions and regulations as may be proper and necessary to carry
into effect the powers granted thereto.
§ 10.10 ORDINANCES REPEALED.
   This code, from and after its effective date, shall contain all of the
provisions of a general nature pertaining to the subjects herein enumerated and
embraced. All prior ordinances pertaining to the subjects treated by this code
shall be deemed repealed from and after the effective date of this code.
§ 10.11 ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature and all other ordinances
pertaining to subjects not embraced in this code shall remain in full force and
effect unless herein repealed expressly or by necessary implication.
§ 10.12 REPEAL OR MODIFICATION OF ORDINANCE.
   (A)   No suit, proceedings, right, fine, forfeiture or penalty instituted,
created, given, secured or accrued under any ordinance previous to its repeal
shall in any way be affected, released or discharged, but may be prosecuted,
enjoyed and recovered as fully as if the ordinance had continued in force
unless it is otherwise expressly provided.
   (B)   When any ordinance repealing a former ordinance, clause or provision
shall be itself repealed, the repeal shall not be construed to revive the
former ordinance, clause or provision, unless it is expressly provided.
§ 10.13 ORDINANCES WHICH AMEND OR SUPPLEMENT CODE.
   (A)   If the legislative body shall desire to amend any existing chapter or
section of this code, the chapter or section shall be specifically repealed and
a new chapter or section, containing the desired amendment, substituted in its
place.
   (B)   Any ordinance which is proposed to add to the existing code a new
chapter or section shall indicate, with reference to the arrangement of this
code, the proper number of the chapter or section. In addition to this
indication as may appear in the text of the proposed ordinance, a caption or
title shall be shown in concise form above the ordinance.
§ 10.14 PRESERVATION OF PENALTIES, OFFENSES, RIGHTS AND LIABILITIES.
   All offenses committed under laws in force prior to the effective date of
this code shall be prosecuted and remain punishable as provided by those laws.
This code does not affect any rights or liabilities accrued, penalties incurred
or proceedings begun prior to the effective date of this code. The liabilities,
proceedings and rights are continued; punishments, penalties or forfeitures
shall be enforced and imposed as if this code had not been enacted. In
particular, any agreement granting permission to utilize highway rights-of-way,
contracts entered into or franchises granted, the acceptance, establishment or
vacation of any highway, and the election of corporate officers shall remain
valid in all respects, as if this code had not been enacted.
§ 10.15 TERRITORIAL APPLICATION OF CODE.
   Except as otherwise provided in this code or by state law, the provisions of
this code shall be applicable in and over all territory within the corporate
limits of the town and any public ground or park belonging to the town, whether
within or without the corporate limits, and in and over all places, except
within the corporate limits of another municipality, within 1 mile of the
corporate limits of the town or of any public ground or park belonging to the
town outside the corporate limits.
Statutory reference:
   Territorial jurisdiction of municipalities, see SDCL § 9-29-1
§ 10.16 LIABILITY OF CORPORATIONS FOR VIOLATIONS.
   For a violation of this code or any other ordinance of the town which, by
nature, does not require intent exercisable only by natural persons, a
corporation may be fined or punished by appropriate penalties in addition to
any punishment provided for its agents who violate this code or other ordinance
while acting as the agents.
§ 10.17 PROSECUTION'S ELECTION WHEN OFFENSE CREATED BY MORE THAN 1 SECTION.
   In all cases where the same offense is made punishable or is created by
different clauses or sections of this code, the prosecuting officer may elect
under which to proceed, but not more than 1 recovery shall be had against the
same person for the same offense; provided, that the revocation of a license or
permit shall not be considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar any other
penalty being enforced.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-10) (Ord. 31, § 1-10, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.18 CONTINUANCE OF TOWN'S RIGHTS AND OBLIGATIONS.
   The town shall continue to own, possess and control all rights and property
of every kind and nature owned, possessed or controlled by it at the time this
Code takes effect, and shall be subject to all its debts, obligations,
liabilities and contracts.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-4) (Ord. 31, § 1-4, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.19 CODE DOES NOT IMPAIR VESTED RIGHTS OR VALID OBLIGATIONS.
   Nothing in this code shall be so construed as to impair any vested rights or
valid obligations existing when it takes effect.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-5) (Ord. 31, § 1-5, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.20 MISCELLANEOUS ORDINANCES NOT AFFECTED BY THE CODE.
   Nothing in this code shall affect the validity of any of the following:
   (A)   Ordinances granting any franchise, right-of-way, easement or contract
right;
   (B)   Ordinances providing for the issuance of bonds, special assessment
certificates, or other evidences of obligations;
   (C)   Ordinances providing for appropriations;
   (D)   Ordinances establishing or changing street grades, widths or names;
   (E)   Any ordinance adopted after the effective date of this 2007 Code of
Ordinances.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-7) (Ord. 31, § 1-7, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.21 POWERS AND AUTHORITIES ARE CUMULATIVE; SEPARABILITY OF PARTS OF CODE.
   Except as otherwise expressly provided, all powers and authorities conferred
by any provision of this code shall be cumulative and additional or, and not in
derogation of, any powers and authorities otherwise existing. Notwithstanding
any other evidence of intent, it is hereby declared to be the controlling
intent of the Board of Trustees that, if any provision of this code or the
application thereof to any persons or circumstances, shall be adjudged by any
court of competent jurisdiction to be invalid, such judgement shall not affect,
impair, or invalidate the remainder of this code, or its application to other
persons and circumstances, but such judgement shall be confined in its
operation to the provisions of the particular chapter, section, subsection or
provision involved, or the application thereof to the persons and circumstances
directly involved in the controversy in which such judgement is rendered.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-11) (Ord. 31, § 1-11, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.22 PUBLICATION AND EFFECT OF CODE.
   This code shall be printed and published in book form and shall take effect
as provided by law.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-14) (Ord. 31, § 1-14, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.23 STATUTE OR LAWS OF THE STATE OF SOUTH DAKOTA.
   Any reference in this code made to the word "statute" or "laws of the State
of South Dakota," or any similar reference, shall refer to the South Dakota
Compiled Laws of 1967, as amended.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-15) (Ord. 31, § 1-14, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 10.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   Whenever in this code or in any ordinance of the town an act is prohibited
or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, or
wherever in such code or ordinance the doing of an act is required, or the
failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful, and no specific penalty is
provided therefor, any person who shall be convicted of any such violation
shall be punished by a fine of not less than $1 nor more than $200, or by
imprisonment for not exceeding 30 days or by both such fine and imprisonment.
Each day any violation of this code or other ordinance continues shall
constitute a separate offense.
(1992 Code, § 5-1-8) (Ord. 31, § 1-8, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Maximum penalty, see SDCL § 9-19-3

§ 30.01 GENERAL PROVISIONS.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees shall consist of 5 members which shall be
elected to office for one 3-year term and one for a one-year term according to
the method provided by the statues of the State of South Dakota.
   (B)   The Board shall be the legislative department of the town government,
and shall perform the duties and have the powers as may be delegated by
statute.
   (C)   The 2 new Board of Trustee positions created by virtue of the
ordinance enacted June 20, 20012, shall be staggered, with one position being
elected to an initial term of 3 years and the other position being selected for
an initial term of one year and 3 years thereafter.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-1) (Ord. 31, § 2-1, passed 10-1-1975; Ord. passed 6-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-1
§ 30.02 TRUSTEES TO QUALIFY FOR OFFICE.
   The members of the Board of Trustees shall qualify and take the oath of
office prescribed by statute, and shall receive the compensations as may be
provided by ordinance.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-2) (Ord. 31, § 2-2, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-1
§ 30.03 ELECTION OF PRESIDENT OF BOARD.
   At the first regular meeting following each election of Trustees, the
Trustees must elect 1 of their members to serve as President of the Board for a
term of 1 year.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 2-3, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-5
§ 30.04 RESPONSIBILITIES OF PRESIDENT.
   The President shall be the presiding officer of all regular and special
meetings of the Board and at all times when the Board meets as a committee of
the whole.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-4) (Ord. 31, § 2-3, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-5
§ 30.05 REGULAR TOWN MEETINGS.
   (A)   The Town Board shall hold its regular and special meetings at the Town
Hall, unless other temporary arrangements are necessary, and then the meetings
shall be held at the place as the Board may designate in the town newspaper at
least 1 week prior to the regular meeting.
   (B)   The regular town meetings shall be held on the first and third
Wednesday of each month.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-5) (Ord. 31, § 2-2, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. 33, passed 3-
23-1977; Am. Ord. passed 7-7-2021)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-6
§ 30.06 CALLING SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   (A)   Special meetings may be called by the President of the Board or any 2
members of the Board upon at least 24 hours notice to all members and the
President.
   (B)   Providing that if all of the Trustees are present at a special
meeting, no notice of the meeting shall be necessary and the notice shall be
deemed waived.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-6) (Ord. 31, § 2-2, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-6
§ 30.07 ORDER OF BUSINESS.
   The order of business of the Board of Trustees of the Town of Keystone shall
be as follows:
   (A)   Call to order;
   (B)   Calling the roll;
   (C)   Reading the minutes;
   (D)   Reports of officers or committees;
   (E)   Notices and communications;
   (F)   Presentations of claims and authorization of warrant issuance;
   (G)   Unfinished business;
   (H)   New business;
   (I)   Other business; and
   (J)   Adjournment.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-7) (Ord. 31, § 2-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch.7
§ 30.08 RESCINDED ACTION.
   No vote or action of the Board of Trustees shall be rescinded at any special
meeting of the Board unless there be present at the special meeting as many
members of the Board as were present at the meeting when the vote or action was
taken.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-8) (Ord. 31, § 2-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 7
§ 30.09 RESOLUTIONS.
   Any resolutions submitted to the Board of Trustees shall be reduced to
writing before being voted upon, upon request of any 2 members of the Board.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-9) (Ord. 31, § 2-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 7
§ 30.10 ADDRESSING THE CHAIR.
   No person shall address the Board until the time as the person shall rise
and address the President and shall have been recognized by the President.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-10) (Ord. 31, § 2-7, passed 10-1-1975) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 7
§ 30.11 SUSPENSION OF RULES OF ORDER.
   The rules of order, other than those prescribed by statute, may be suspended
at any time by the consent of a majority of the members present at the meeting.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-11) (Ord. 31, § 2-8, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 7
§ 30.12 PARLIAMENTARY RULES.
   Roberts Rules of Order, revised, shall govern the deliberation of the Board
of Trustees except when in conflict with any of the foregoing rules.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-12) (Ord. 31, § 2-9, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 7
§ 30.13 QUORUM.
   A majority of the Trustees shall constitute a quorum to do business, but no
action shall be taken without a majority of the Board of Trustees approving the
actions.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-13) (Ord. 31, § 2-10, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-7-7
§ 30.14 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   The Board of Trustees shall have the power to create committees for the
purpose of gathering information, analyzing and overseeing certain activities
for the benefit of the Board. All committees shall consist of 3 members each, 1
of which members shall be a Trustee. The President of the Board of Trustees
shall appoint all committee members and at the request of a majority of the
Board of Trustees, any report of a committee may be deferred for final action
until the next regular meeting of the Board.
(1992 Code, § 1-1-14) (Ord. 31, § 2-11, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch.7
§ 30.15 LIMITING TERMS.
   The term limit of a Trustee, including the Board President, shall be 2 terms
beginning the first city meeting in May after its election. No Trustee may
serve more than 2 consecutive elected terms.
(Ord. 1-2-17, passed 5-15-2002; Am. Ord. passed 11-18-2015)

FINANCE OFFICER
§ 31.01 APPOINTMENT.
   There shall be appointed a Finance Officer instead of an Auditor, Clerk and
Treasurer. The Finance Officer shall perform all of the duties of the Auditor,
Clerk and Treasurer as provided by state law, except where duplicate records
are required, only 1 set of records will be necessary. The Finance Officer
shall be bonded as required by state law for the Treasurer.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-1) (Ord. 31, § 4-1, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.02 TERM OF OFFICE.
   The Finance Officer shall be appointed at the first regular meeting in May
of each year, and shall subscribe an oath or affirmation of office as required
by state law.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-2) (Ord. 31, § 4-2, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. passed 7-7-
2021)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.03 AMOUNT OF BOND.
   The bond shall be annually established by the Board of Trustees in an amount
equal to the maximum amount estimated to be on hand at any 1 time, but not to
exceed $50,000.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-3) (Ord. 31, § 4-3, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.04 GENERAL DUTIES.
   The Finance Officer shall:
   (A)   Keep his or her office at the place as the Board of Trustees may
direct, and keep the corporate seal and all papers and records of the town;
   (B)   Draw and countersign all warrants on the Treasury in pursuance of
orders or resolutions of the Board and keep a full and accurate account thereof
in books provided for that purpose;
   (C)   Make, or cause to be made, estimates of the expenses for any work to
be done by the town, countersign all contracts made on its behalf and
certificates of work authorized by any committee of the Board by any town
officer;
   (D)   Keep regular books of accounts in which he or she shall enter all
indebtedness of the town, and which shall at all times show the financial
condition of the town, the amount of bonds, warrants, certificates or other
evidences of indebtedness which have been redeemed, and the amount of each
outstanding;
   (E)   Countersign all bonds, warrants or other evidences of indebtedness of
the town and keep accurate accounts thereof, stating to whom and for what
purpose issued, and the amount thereof;
   (F)   Keep an account with all receiving and disbursing officers of the
town, showing the amount they have received from the different sources of
revenue and the amount which they have disbursed under the direction of the
Board;
   (G)   Supervise the accounting system for all departments and offices of the
town in accordance with the recommendations of the State Department of Audits
and Accounts;
   (H)   Keep a list of all certificates issued for work or any other purpose;
and before the levy by the Board of any special tax shall, unless that duty is
performed by the Engineer, report to the Board a schedule of all lots which may
be subject to the proposed special tax of assessment, which it may be necessary
to levy on the lots, which schedule shall be verified by his or her affidavit;
   (I)   Examine all reports, books, papers, vouchers and accounts of the
Treasury;
   (J)   Audit and adjust all claims and demands against the town before they
are allowed by the Board;
   (K)   Keep a record of his or her acts and doings;
   (L)   Keep a book in which he or she shall enter all contracts with an index
thereto, which book shall be open in the inspection of all parties interested;
and
   (M)   Perform other duties as may be required by ordinance, resolution or
direction of the Board.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-4) (Ord. 31, § 4-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.05 DUTY TO ATTEND BOARD MEETINGS AND KEEP RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS.
   The Finance Officer shall attend all meetings of the Board of Trustees and
keep a record of its proceedings.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-5) (Ord. 31, § 4-5, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.06 PREPARATION AND KEEPING OF BOND LIST.
   The Finance Officer shall make and keep a list of outstanding town bonds, to
whom issued, for what purpose, when and where payable and the rate of interest
they respectively bear.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-6) (Ord. 31, § 4-6, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.07 ANNUAL FINANCIAL REPORT.
   The Finance Officer shall report to the Board, on the first day of January
of each year, the receipts, expenses and financial condition of the town, which
report shall be published within 30 days thereafter in the official paper, or
the other paper as the Board may direct.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-7) (Ord. 31, § 4-7, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
§ 31.08 ANNUAL INVENTORY.
   The Financial Officer shall report to the Board, on January 1 of each year,
an inventory of all supplies, both office and equipment on hand, which
inventory shall also include the Police Department.
(1992 Code, § 1-2-8) (Ord. 31, § 4-8, passed 10-1-1975)

   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-14
MUNICIPAL ATTORNEY
§ 31.25 APPOINTMENT.
   There is hereby created the Office of Municipal Attorney, an executive
office of the town. The Attorney shall be appointed by the Board of Trustees.

Statutory reference:

§ 31.26 DUTIES.
   (A)   The Attorney shall prosecute or defend any or all actions or suits at
law, equity to which the town may be a party, or in which it may be interested,
or which may be brought against, or by an officer of the town, on behalf of the
town or in the capacity of the person as an officer of the town.
   (B)   The Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the town and shall render
advice on all legal questions affecting the town, whenever requested to do so
by any town official. Upon request by the President of the Board of Trustees,
he or she shall reduce the opinion to writing.

§ 31.61 GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES. 
   The Health Officer shall have and exercise a general supervision over the
sanitary conditions of the town. He or she shall give the Board of Trustees all
the professional advice and information as they may require in regard to the
public health. He or she shall enforce all the laws of the state relative to
sanitary matters and all ordinances of the town bearing on public health.

PARKS AND RECREATION BOARD
§ 32.01 BOARD CREATED.
   There is hereby created a Parks and Recreation Board for the town, to be
known as the Keystone Parks and Recreation Board, to establish, improve, care
for, regulate and manage a system of public parks, zoological park, parkways
and boulevards and to operate a system of public recreation, playgrounds and
children's parks in and for the Town of Keystone.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-1) (Ord. 50, § 1, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.02 COMPENSATION OF BOARD.
   The Parks and Recreation Board shall be composed of 5 members, each of whom
shall be a resident of the town.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-2) (Ord. 50, § 2, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.03 BOARD MEMBERS NOT TO BE ELECTIVE OFFICERS.
   The members of the Parks and Recreation Board shall not hold any elective
office in the government of the town.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-3) (Ord. 50, § 3, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.04 APPOINTMENT BY BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   The members of the Parks and Recreation Board shall be appointed by the
Board of Trustees, at its first regular meeting in May of each year.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-4) (Ord. 50, § 4, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.05 TERMS OF APPOINTMENT.
   Of the members appointed initially to the Parks and Recreation Board, all
shall be subject to reappointment on the first meeting date of each May.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-5) (Ord. 50, § 5, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.06 VACANCIES ON BOARD.
   Any vacancy on the town Parks and Recreation Board, shall be filled for the
unexpired term of the member vacating the Board in the same manner as is
required for a regular appointment, and shall also qualify for the position as
provided above.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-6) (Ord. 50, § 6, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.07 QUALIFICATIONS OF MEMBERS.
   Each member of the Board, before entering upon his or her official duties,
shall give bond to the town in the amount of $500, if required by the Board of
Trustees, for the faithful performance of his or her duties and shall take and
file in the Town Auditor’s office with the bond, the usual oath of office
required from appointive officers of the town. The town shall pay any premium
for the bonds required to be given members of the Board or its officers or
employees. All official bonds required under the provisions of this section
shall be approved by the Board of Trustees.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-7) (Ord. 50, § 7, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.08 OFFICERS.
   At the first regular meeting of the Parks and Recreation Board in May of
each year, the Board shall elect from its number, a President, Vice President
and a Secretary, each of whom shall serve until the first meeting of the Board
in May of the following year. The Vice President shall act in the absence or
disability of the President. In case of death or retirement of an officer, a
successor shall be elected immediately.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-8) (Ord. 50, § 8, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.09 MEETINGS.
   The Parks and Recreation Board shall hold regular meetings at least once
each month and as many special meetings as it deems proper.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-9) (Ord. 50, § 9, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.10 QUORUM.
   Three members of the Parks and Recreation Board shall constitute a quorum
for the transaction of business.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-10) (Ord. 50, § 10, passed 12-16-1981; Am. Ord. 1-6-10,
passed 2-16-1994)
§ 32.11 AFFIRMATIVE ACTION VOTE.
   An affirmative vote of at least a majority of the voting members of the
Parks and Recreation Board shall be necessary to authorize any action of the
Board.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-11) (Ord. 50, § 11, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.12 RECORDS AND REPORTS.
   The Secretary of the Parks and Recreation Board shall keep a record of its
proceedings and make the reports as may be required by the Board. In his or her
absence or inability to act, the Board may appoint a Secretary Pro-Tem to
perform his or her duties. The records of the Board, kept by its Secretary or
copies of any records when duly certified by the Secretary, shall be competent
evidence of the proceedings of the Board.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-12) (Ord. 50, § 12, passed 12-16-1981)
§ 32.13 POWERS, DUTIES AND LIMITATIONS.
   The Parks and Recreation Board shall have all of those powers and duties and
be subject to the limitations and enjoy those privileges and immunities all as
provided by state law. Whenever the prior approval of the Board of Trustees is
required before the Board can act, the prior approval shall be first obtained.
(1992 Code, § 1-6-13) (Ord. 50, § 12, passed 12-16-1981)
LIBRARY BOARD
§ 32.50 LIBRARY BOARD CREATED.
   There is hereby created for the Town of Keystone, a Library Board to be
known as the Keystone Town Library Board.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 14-2-28
§ 32.51 COMPOSITION OF BOARD.
   The Library Board shall be composed of 5 members, each of whom shall be a
resident of the county within the servicing area.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.52 BOARD MEMBERS NOT TO BE ELECTIVE OFFICERS.
   The members of the Keystone Library Board shall not hold any elective office
in the government of the town.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.53 APPOINTMENT AND TERMS OF OFFICE.
   Any public library established under SDCL § 14-2-29(1) shall be governed by
a board of public library trustees. The governing body shall appoint 5
competent citizens broadly representative of the population of the local
governmental unit. One of the citizens shall be appointed for 1 year, 2 for 2
years, and 2 for 3 years and annually thereafter reappointments or new
appointments shall be for a term of 3 years or to complete an unexpired term.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 14-2-35
§ 32.54 FILLING VACANCY ON BOARD.
   In case of any vacancy in membership of the Library Board due to death,
resignation or otherwise, a successor shall be appointed to fill the unexpired
portion of the term of the member he or she replaces. If a member of the
Library Board fails to attend 3 consecutive meetings, his or her seat on the
Board shall be termed vacant.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.55 OFFICERS.
   At the first regular meeting of the Library Board in May of each year, the
Board shall elect from its number, a Chairperson of the Board and Vice
Chairperson, each of whom shall serve until the first meeting of the Board in
May of the following year. The Vice Chairperson shall act in the absence or
disability of the Chairperson. In case of death or retirement of an officer, a
successor shall be elected immediately.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.56 MEETINGS.
   The Library Board shall hold regular meetings at least once each month and
as many special meetings as it deems proper.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.57 QUORUM.
   Three members of the Library Board shall constitute a quorum for the
transaction of business.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.58 AFFIRMATIVE ACTION VOTE.
   An affirmative vote of at least a majority of the voting members of the
Library Board shall be necessary to authorize any action of the Board.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.59 RECORDS AND REPORTS.
   The KCC/Library employee shall keep a record of its proceedings and make the
reports as may be required by the Board. In his or her absence or inability to
act, the Board may appoint a Secretary Pro-Tem to perform his or her duties.
The records of the Board, kept by the Finance Office or copies of any records
when duly certified by the library employee, shall be competent evidence of the
proceedings of the Board.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.60 POWERS, DUTIES AND LIMITATIONS.
   The Library Board shall have all of those powers and duties and be subject
to the limitations and enjoy those privileges and immunities all as provided by
state law.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
§ 32.61 REPORTS TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   The Board shall make a report to the Board of Trustees every month, and at
other times as the Board of Trustees may direct.
(Ord. passed 2-5-2014)
CHAPTER 33: PURCHASING PROCEDURES
Section
   
33.01   Town department heads and officers authorized to make purchases
   
33.02   Requisitions
   
33.03   Disposition of purchase order and copies
   
33.04   From whom purchase to be made
   
33.05   Town not liable for improper purchases
   
33.06   Charge for insufficient funds checks
   
33.07   Fees paid by credit/debit machine
§ 33.01 TOWN DEPARTMENT HEADS AND OFFICERS AUTHORIZED TO MAKE PURCHASES.
   All town department heads and officers are authorized to spend municipal
funds to purchase supplies, equipment, inventory, services, or similar expenses
for and on behalf of the town during any calendar month, not exceeding $2,000
in the aggregate. In the event such expenses will exceed $2,000 during the
calendar month, the town department head or officer shall obtain prior approval
and authorization from the Board of Trustees.
(1992 Code, § 1-3-1) (Ord. 31, § 9-1, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. 1-3-1a, passed
6-7-2006; Am. Ord. passed 5-2-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-12-1
§ 33.02 REQUISITIONS.
   (A)   Whenever any town department head or officer desires to make any
purchase in excess of $100 for materials, supplies, equipment, printing or
services on behalf of the town, he or she shall execute a purchase order
therefor in triplicate, setting forth thereon the item to be purchased, the
department for which the item is purchased and the source of supply.
   (B)   If approval from a Trustee is required, it shall be submitted for his
or her signature prior to making any purchase.
(1992 Code, § 1-3-2) (Ord. 31, § 9-2, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 33.03 DISPOSITION OF PURCHASE ORDER AND COPIES.
   (A)   The original purchase order shall be delivered to the supplier, who
shall be requested to attach the same to his or her invoice when rendered to
the town for payment.
   (B)   The duplicate copy shall be delivered to the Finance Officer within 1
working day of the purchase.
   (C)   The triplicate copy shall be retained by the department head or
officer in his or her permanent records.
(1992 Code, § 1-3-3) (Ord. 31, § 9-3, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 33.04 FROM WHOM PURCHASE TO BE MADE.
   When a requisition and expenditure requested thereby is authorized as
provided for in this section, the purchase shall be made from a contractor who
has made a contract to supply the items as are required by the requisition, if
the town has entered into the contract. If the town does not have any contract
for the purchase of the type or kind of items required in the requisition, the
purchase shall be made from any supplier upon the direction of the department
head or officer, and the department head or officer shall use his or her best
efforts to obtain the lowest satisfactory price and terms for the purchase.
(1992 Code, § 1-3-4) (Ord. 31, § 9-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 33.05 TOWN NOT LIABLE FOR IMPROPER PURCHASES.
   The town shall not be liable for any supplies, materials or equipment,
purchased or contracted for in violation of this chapter.
(1992 Code, § 1-3-5) (Ord. 31, § 9-5, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 33.06 CHARGE FOR INSUFFICIENT FUNDS CHECK.
   (A)   A charge of $30 will be added to any insufficient fund check that is
returned to the town.
   (B)   The amount of the insufficient fund check and the $30 charge must be
paid in full before any services will be continued.
(Ord. 5-1-16, passed 5-4-2005; Am. Ord. passed 5-4-2011; Am. Ord. passed 11-6-
2011)
§ 33.07 FEES PAID BY CREDIT/DEBIT MACHINE.
   The Town of Keystone is authorized to accept payment for any fees due to the
Town of Keystone in form of payment by credit/debit card machine. If payment is
made using credit/debit, a fee of 5% shall be added to any such payment.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2011)
CHAPTER 34: ANNUAL CONTRACT PROCEDURE
Section
   
34.01   Estimate statements
   
34.02   Pre-auditing and approval of estimate statements
   
34.03   Notice for bids; bidder’s security
   
34.04   Opening and accepting or rejecting bids
   
34.05   Written contracts required; with exception
§ 34.01 ESTIMATE STATEMENTS.
   On August 1 of each calendar year, each officer or employee of the town in
charge of any department or office shall furnish to the Board of Trustees, in
duplicate, a detailed statement of the estimated services and supplies which
will be needed by the department or office during the next calendar year. One
copy of the statement shall be forthwith supplied by the President of the Board
of Trustees to the purchasing agent.
(1992 Code, § 1-4-1) (Ord. 31, § 8-1, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 34.02 PRE-AUDITING AND APPROVAL OF ESTIMATE STATEMENTS.
   The Board and the purchasing agent shall pre-audit and examine the
statements of estimates furnished pursuant to this section and shall determine
upon the amount and character of supplies to be purchased, and for which bids
shall be requested. When the estimate statements have been so pre- audited, the
Board shall submit the same for approval by a majority vote.
(1992 Code, § 1-4-2) (Ord. 31, § 8-2, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-12-1, 9-12-2
§ 34.03 NOTICE FOR BIDS; BIDDER’S SECURITY.
   Upon approval of the estimate statements by the Board of Trustees, as
provided for in this section, the Finance Officer shall publish a notice for
bids to be published 3 consecutive weeks prior to the time fixed for opening
bids, in the official newspaper of the town. The notice for bids shall contain
notice that bidders, in their bids, shall undertake to supply the town with the
services or supplies indicated in the notice and from time to time upon
purchase orders by the purchasing agent for the ensuing calendar year. The
Board of Trustees, at the time of directing notice for bids, shall specify the
type of security, if any, to be given by the bidder.
(1992 Code, § 1-4-3) (Ord. 31, § 8-3, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-12-1
§ 34.04 OPENING AND ACCEPTING OR REJECTING BIDS.
   Bids received pursuant to the notice provided for in this chapter shall be
opened by the Board prior to the close of the current calendar year and
referred to the purchasing agent for investigation and for report and
recommendation back to the Board, whereupon the Board shall accept the lowest
bid of a responsible bidder, taking into consideration the character and
quality of the goods to be furnished and the facilities of the bidder to
deliver the supplies, materials, equipment or services in accordance with the
requirements of the town. The Board may reject any or all bids and may re-
advertise notices for further bids.
(1992 Code, § 1-4-4) (Ord. 31, § 8-4, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-12-2
§ 34.05 WRITTEN CONTRACTS REQUIRED; WITH EXCEPTION.
   (A)   Written contracts shall be entered into with successful bidders unless
delivery is to be made forthwith. The Board may direct any local improvement,
except where special assessments are to be levied, to be done by day's work if
the reasonable cost thereof is not in excess of $1,500. An estimate of the cost
shall be prepared by the Engineer and filed in the Town Hall for public
inspection at least 5 days before the improvement is directed.
   (B)   Upon completion of the improvement, the Finance Officer shall prepare
and file, forthwith, for public inspection, in his or her office, an itemized
statement of the cost paid out in the construction of the improvement, verified
by him or her.
(1992 Code, § 1-4-5) (Ord. 31, § 8-5, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-12-2
CHAPTER 35: TAXATION
