§ 53.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purposes of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   APPROVING AUTHORITY. The town’s representative or its duly authorized
deputy, agent or representative.
   NOTICE. A notice in writing directed to the owner of or other person
affected for the time specified by this section, stating briefly the condition
which is the reason for the notice and the consequences which would result upon
failure to comply with the terms of the notice. A NOTICE shall be deemed given
when either it is personally served on the person to whom it is directed or is
mailed to him or her at his or her last known address. If the owner cannot be
reached by mail so addressed, service may be made upon the occupant.
   PERSON. An individual, corporation (public or private), partnership or
association.
   PUBLIC WATER. A common water controlled by public authority.
   RESIDENTIAL USER. A single-family unit.
   SERVICE. Connection to the municipal water system and the right to the use
of its facilities whether or not the facilities are in fact used.
   TOWN. The Town of Keystone or its officers or employees authorized to
perform the functions to which there is reference.
   USER. The owner, lessee or occupant of the premises connected to the
municipal water system.
   WATER SYSTEM. The network of appurtenances for the collection, distribution
and pumping of water.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.02 WATER DEPARTMENT.
   The Water Department shall be under the supervision of the Public Works
Supervisor, who shall be responsible to the town Board of Trustees. The
Supervisor or any employee of the Water Department, shall be permitted at all
reasonable hours to enter the premises or buildings of consumers for the
purposes of reading meters, examining water pipes, shutting off water from
residences or businesses for non-payment. The Supervisor shall be permitted to
turn on or off water connections due to breaks or damage. The Supervisor shall
make a written report to the Board of Trustees prior to each regular meeting of
the Board of Trustees covering the work completed. This report shall include
all new water connections, new lines constructed, repairs and necessary
replacements made, the number of hours worked and he or she shall make the
recommendations as seem proper for the efficient operation of the water system
and improvements of the same.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.03 GUARDING EXCAVATION SITES.
   All excavations for water installations shall be adequately guarded with
barricades and lights and other appropriate warning devises so as to protect
the public from hazard. Streets, alleys, sidewalks and other public property
disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory
to the town. Any excavations will take into consideration confined spaces
safety protocol.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.04 PLAT OF WATER MAINS.
   The Public Works Water Department shall keep and maintain a plat on which
shall be shown a complete diagram of all town mains, the size of the mains, and
other information as shall be deemed advisable by the Public Works Supervisor.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.05 INTERFERING WITH FIRE HYDRANTS.
   Only employees of the town or members of a Fire Department shall open, take
any water from, or in any way interfere with any public fire hydrant in the
town. Fire hydrants shall be kept free of any obstruction that would limit a
Fire Department’s access to the hydrant.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.06 PLUMBERS.
   (A)   Only a duly licensed plumber or an employee of the Public Works Water
Department shall be permitted to do any work on any pipes of connections in any
way connected to the town water supply.
   (B)   All plumbers shall be governed by state and town regulations that are
currently in force or that may be hereafter adopted.
   (C)   No person, including, but not limited to, plumbers, property owners
and tenants shall turn water on or off at curb stops unless they have received
written permission from the town Finance Officer.
   (D)   In the case of an emergency water turn off, the town must be notified
within three days of the turnoff.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.07 USE OF MUNICIPAL WATER SYSTEM REQUIRED.
   As per SDCL § 9-47-28, the owner of every residence, business, structure or
building wherein water is used, abutting upon any street or alley in which
municipal water mains are maintained shall, at his or her own expense, connect
the residence, business, structure or building to the municipal water system
within 30 days after notice to do so, provided the municipal water main is
within 200 feet of his or her property line.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.08 WATER DEPOSIT.
   All owners or occupants using municipal water, including but not limited to
home, commercial and industrial facilities, shall pay a deposit of $75 if
residence or $100 if commercial/industrial, before commencement of service to a
new party in a unit already served. The deposit will be refunded after 1 year
if the party has kept current with the bill. If deposit has been refunded, a
new deposit shall be required if service is disconnected for non-payment. The
deposit requirement is to ensure payment for use of water.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.09 COMMERCIAL AND RESIDENTIAL USES DEFINED.
   (A)   COMMERCIAL USE. Includes but is not limited to, the following uses to
wit:
      (1)   Retail stores, sales and display rooms and shops;
      (2)   Offices;
      (3)   Financial institutions;
      (4)   Eating and drinking establishments, including drive-in
establishments;
      (5)   Personal service establishments;
      (6)   Business service establishments;
      (7)   Commercial, job and newspaper printing;
      (8)   Establishments offering repair services on items brought in by
customers;
      (9)   Amusement and recreation establishments;
      (10)   Private business schools, studios and vocational schools;
      (11)   Private or public clubs and lodges;
      (12)   Any other store or shop for retail trade or rendering personal,
professional or business service;
      (13)   Apartment buildings;
      (14)   Retail and distribution establishments, including the manufacture,
compounding, processing, packaging or treatment of products for human
consumption; sales and display rooms and lots, not including yards for storage
of new or used building materials or yards for any scrap or salvage operations,
or for storage or display of any scrap, salvage or secondhand materials;
      (15)   Hotels, motels, rooming and boarding houses and restaurants;
      (16)   Commercial recreational structures and uses, such as theaters,
bowling alleys and pool rooms;
      (17)   Offices, studios, clinics and laboratories;
      (18)   Art galleries and museums;
      (19)   Business and vocational schools not involving operations of an
Industrial character;
      (20)   Elementary or secondary schools, public or private;
      (21)   Libraries, museums and historical monuments or structures;
      (22)   Nursing homes or homes for the aged;
      (23)   Mobile home parks; and
      (24)   Automotive service stations.
   (B)   RESIDENTIAL USES. Includes any use not otherwise defined as a
commercial use under §
53.09(A) or any use by a non-profit corporation or non-profit legal entity and
such non-profit legal status is recognized under the Federal Internal Revenue
Code.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022; Am. Ord. passed 3-1-2023)
§ 53.10 WATER USERS OUTSIDE OF TOWN LIMITS.
   (A)   All users of water service supplied by the town waterworks outside the
town limits, shall be governed by all rules, regulations and ordinances in
effect with the town concerning the same, and shall be charged rates as
determined by the Board of Trustees.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person living outside the town limits of
the town, to connect to the Keystone water without a written contract with the
town.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.11 ACCOUNT MUST BE PAID BEFORE WATER TURNED ON.
   (A)   No person or business shall be permitted re-connection to the water
system until all past water accounts are fully paid. Notice for water service
must be made to the Finance Officer 1 day prior for the service.
   (B)   A fee of $20 shall be charged for each account when completed during
regular business, Monday through Friday, and a fee of $50 shall be charged for
the service to be done before 8:00 a.m. or after 3:00 p.m.
   (C)   There will be no weekend service unless an emergency occurs. Owners of
the property, or their agents, must give notice of changes to tenants or
parties responsible for water consumption, or the owners shall be responsible
for charges incurred for water consumption.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.12 SPRINKLING.
   The use of water for street, lawn or garden sprinkling is subordinate to
domestic use or fire protection and may be restricted by the town at any time
by resolution of the Board of Trustees. No sprinkling shall be done during a
fire.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.13 MORE THAN 1 CONSUMER FROM 1 SERVICE.
   (A)   Each plat will have its own service line. If 2 residences or buildings
are located on the same plan each residence or building will have its own
service line.
   (B)   Owners who lease or the person in whose name the account is
registered, shall be responsible for water used in the premises.
   (C)   If more than 1 meter is placed on a service line, the meter closest to
the curbstop shall be considered the master meter for billing and usage
purposes.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.14 EXTENSION OF WATER PIPES.
   (A)   (1)   Plumbers must not extend water pipes from 1 premises to another.
      (2)   All connection with the municipal water mains must have a curbstop
and backflow preventor boxes to be located within a meter pit within 1 foot of
the property line of the property to be served on the public right of way or
public easement.
   (B)   Design criteria.
      (1)   Water mains will be required to meet the Handbook of PVC Pipe
Design, Unibell, current edition and South Dakota DANR Standards.
      (2)   Recommended Standards for Water Works, “Ten States Standards”,
current edition.
      (3)   National Standard Plumbing Code Illustrated, current edition.
      (4)   Minimum service line size is 1 inch.
      (5)   Tapping saddles and corporation stops are required. Tapping and all
materials are the responsibility of the contractor. Town Public Works
Supervisor shall observe all water main taps. The contractor shall contact and
schedule the proposed tap with Keystone Public Works 2 days prior to the
anticipated tap.
      (6)   Tapping saddles shall be solid band 304 stainless -steel
construction with stainless-steel nuts and bolts. Tapered Buna-N ASTM D-2000
rubber gasketed (Ford FS303 or equal).
      (7)   Compression type connections with inserts are required. (No yellow
brass allowed. Red brass only.)
      (8)   No service line splices on any section of the line.
      (9)   Curb stop valves must be a type with a cylindrical plug provided
with a pressure activated “O” ring sealed in a machine groove near the top of
the plug. Curb stop valves shall be Muller Mark II Driseal No H-15154, Hayes
Nuseal No 4012 or equivalent. Drains shall not be permitted on the valves.
      (10)   Curb boxes shall be cast iron that telescope to a length of 6
feet, have a Minneapolis Pattern base and screw type lid marked “Water” with a
pentagon brass nut. Risers shall be a minimum of 1 inches in diameter. Curb
boxes shall be Muller-H10300 or equivalent.
      (11)   Water services shall be bedded with fines according to bedding
specifications for crusher fines with a minimum 3 inches below the pipe and 3
inches above the pipe.
      (12)   Select soil material is required for a minimum of 18 inches above
the pipe and shall include no rocks 2 inches or larger in normal diameter.
      (13)   The service line excavation within the public right-of-way or
public easement shall be compacted to the satisfaction of the town. Excavation
settlement and subsequent damages resulting therefrom shall be the
responsibility of the user for a period of 1 year.
      (14)   The cost of original installation of all pipes and plumbing
between the municipal service mains and the user’s curb stop and all extensions
thereto and any sewer and water lines shall be borne by the user entirely. All
such plumbing and service installations shall at all times be subject to
inspection by the Public Works Supervisor. Upon final inspection of the
installation, the service line and curb stop located in the public right of way
shall become the property of the municipality.
      (15)   All water service lines shall be tested for leakage by a licensed
plumber and inspected by the town prior to back filling of the service line
excavation. The testing method shall be approved by the town prior to
conducting the test. A minimum notice of at least 24 hours is required prior to
any inspection.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.15 RIGHT-OF-WAY REPAIR.
   The user shall be responsible for the repair and restoration of any
excavation done to install or repair service lines, public right-of-way or
public easements. All back fill and surface repair shall be done to the
satisfaction of the town.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.16 NOTICE OF DISCONTINUANCE REQUIRED.
   (A)   Customers desiring to discontinue the use of water shall be required
to give 1 day notice prior to the shut off service to the town Finance Officer.
   (B)   Regular rate shall be continued until the notice is given. Account
must be paid in full prior to the shut off request. A fee of $20 shall be
charged for the request when completed during regular business Monday through
Friday, and a fee of $50 shall be charged for the service to turn on or off the
water before 8:00 a.m. or after 3:00 p.m.
   (C)   There will be no shut off service on weekends unless an emergency
occurs. Owners of the property or his or her agent must give notice of changes
of tenants or parties responsible for water consumption or the owners shall be
responsible for charges incurred for water consumption.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.17 REQUIRED CAPPING OF LINES.
   (A)   Any owner of property upon which any structure is removed, demolished
or raised shall be responsible for capping any sanitary sewer lines and water
lines. Said lines shall be capped at the point where the structure’s service
line is tapped into the town main.
   (B)   The procedure for capping shall be approved by the Public Works
Supervisor.
   (C)   All caps shall be inspected by the Public Works Supervisor before any
trench being filled and compacted.
   (D)   A minimum of 24-hour notice shall be given for inspections.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.18 SURETY BONDS AND INSURANCE REQUIRED OF APPLICANT.
   The applicant shall indemnify and save harmless the town from any claims of
injury, loss or damage to third parties arising out of the construction work.
This provision is a condition of the issuance of the permit. The town may, as a
condition to the issuance of the permit, require the applicant to file a
corporate surety bond for a period of 2 years.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.19 EMERGENCY WATER LIMITATIONS.
   The Supervisor may, with the consent of the Board of Trustees, limit or
prohibit temporarily the use of town water for any purpose in an emergency.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.20 RESPONSIBILITY FOR BREAKAGE OF LINES.
   (A)   The town shall have authority to close the curb stop at any time a
break in the service line appears to have occurred, and will reopen the curb
stop when satisfied that no break exists or the break has been repaired. In a
case where a property owner wishes to update or breaks have occurred, the owner
may be eligible for the city to pay for half of a manufactured meter pit to be
installed at the lot line. If owners wish to receive partial compensation for a
meter pit, they must come before the Town Board for approval.
   (B)   In the event of breakage of a water line between the lot line and the
residence, business or structure, the person having ownership or responsibility
for the premises shall be responsible for the maintenance or repair of the line
from the lot line to the residence, business or structure, and the town shall
have responsibility for breakage or repair from the lot line to the main.
   (C)   It is understood the owners or responsible party of the property shall
be responsible for the repairs as stated in order to preserve the street and
sewer and water systems of the city.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.21 MALICIOUS OR WILLFUL DAMAGE TO THE WATER SYSTEM.
   No person shall maliciously or willfully break, damage or tamper with any
water main, meter, structure, devise or equipment which is part of the
municipal water system.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.22 WATER METERS.
   (A)   All dwellings or places supplied with water from the town water system
shall be metered.
   (B)   A suitable place for meters, safe from frost or other damage and
accessible for examination, must be provided by and at the expense of the owner
or occupant. In any case where the meter is injured by freezing or otherwise
damaged by act or neglect of the owner or occupant, it shall be repaired or
replaced, and the expense thereof shall be paid by the owner or occupant of the
premises. In case of neglect, refusal to repair/replace or refusal to pay
expenses thereof, the water supply may be turned off and not turned on until
the costs and a reconnect fee have been paid.
   (C)   The town will supply meters 3/4-inch and smaller to all accounts where
applicable so meters are compatible with the town’s computer read system.
Customers are responsible for the reimbursement to the town for all meters
supplied.
   (D)   All accounts are responsible for their own installation, regardless of
size of meter; commercial accounts requiring meters larger than 3/4-inch are
required to purchase their own meters which are compatible with the town’s
computer read system.
   (E)   Manufactured meter pits shall be required for all new construction
that uses residential sized meters and shall be located within 1 foot of the
users lot line where possible or in a place designated by the Public Works
supervisor where lot line placement is not feasible.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.23 PORTABLE METER SPECIAL WATER USERS PERMIT.
   (A)   The Supervisor shall provide 1 or more portable water meters for any
special temporary use where water is taken from a service line. A permit shall
first be obtained and shall specify the place from which water is to be taken,
the quantity to be taken, the purpose of which the water is to be used and if a
charge is to be made for the water, it shall be paid. When a charge is made, a
portable meter shall be attached to the tap from which the water is to be
taken, the regular water rate shall be charged or the rate as may be fixed by
the Board of Trustees, plus a connect fee except when otherwise fixed by the
Board of Trustees. The meter shall be read when other meters are read, or
sooner if the use of the water is discontinued.
   (B)   Customers of the portable hydrant meter will have to pay a $100
deposit, and a $50 non-refundable charge to use the meter. Customers will also
have to sign an agreement that if the meter is damaged or lost, the customer is
responsible for the full cost of a new replacement meter.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.24 TESTING METERS ON REQUEST OF CONSUMER.
   Upon written request of an owner or other person liable for the payment for
water used on the premises, the Water Department will test the meter supplying
the premises after a disconnection fee is paid. The person requesting the test
may be present when the test is made, and in all cases the Superintendent will
report the results. If an excess of 2% on a flow equal to 1/8 of the diameter
of the service or greater is found, the dollar fee will be refunded as well as
a 2 month credit or charge based on water used during the past 2 months only.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.25 METERS FAILING TO REGISTER.
   In cases where meters shall fail to register the amount of water used,
charges shall be based on the average used during the 2 or more preceding years
of similar length and during a similar time of the year.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
§ 53.26 TAP AND CONNECTION CHARGES.
   (A)   (1)   Any person desiring residential water or sewer service shall
apply for connection on a form provided by the municipality and the application
shall be filed with the Finance Officer, together with a $1,000 fee for water
tap and $1,000 fee for sewer tap. The fee shall be returned if the application
is rejected. Any person desiring commercial sewer and water shall pay a fee of
$2,000 for water tap and $2,000 for sewer tap and shall apply as hereinbefore
set forth.
      (2)   The fee shall entitle the applicant to connect with the water or
sewer main at the applicant’s expense, provided that the connection shall be
made under the supervision of the Water and Sewer Superintendent and inspected
as herein provided.
   (B)   There will be an additional impact fee of $25 per fixture such as
toilets, showers, faucets, and laundry rooms to be added to the application.
The monies received shall be deposited into the water and sewer reserve
accounts.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.27 WATER CHARGES.
   (A)    There shall be charged by the town effective immediately upon passage
and publication as provided by law, a water charge for service to persons,
association of persons, partnerships, corporations, firms and legal entities
based upon usage as follows:
 
Base Rate for Residential Base Rate for Commercial
$15.50                    $19.00
 
 
Gallons                Rate
0 - 2,000 gallons      Base rate
2,001 - 5,000 gallons  $10.50 per 1,000
5,001 - 7,000 gallons  $11.00 per 1,000
7,001 - 10,000 gallons $12.25 per 1,000
10,000 gallons & up    $11.75 per 1,000
Yearly increase thereafter in the amount of $0.50 each increment.
 
   (B)   All residential and commercial/industrial water charges shall be paid
monthly.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022; Am. Ord. passed 3-1-2023)
§ 53.28 BILLING AND PAYMENTS.
   All bills for utility services furnished by the town shall be due and
payable on the thirtieth of each month. If the payment is not in City Hall by
3:00 pm on the thirtieth of each month, the customer will be charged a $20
residential, $40 commercial/industrial late fee. In the event the bill is not
paid by the tenth of the following month (a grace period ) water will be shut
off until the past due and late charge amount is paid in full. Water services
will be reconnected upon payment in full of past due and late charge amount
plus $50 residential and $100 commercial/industrial reconnect fee has been
paid. Special circumstances will be dealt with by Board of Trustees.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022) Penalty, see §
53.99
§ 53.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Except as otherwise provided herein, any person violating any
provision of this chapter shall be subjected to 30 days imprisonment in a
county jail or $500 fine, or both. In addition to the sentence that is imposed
herein, the defendant shall make restitution to the town.
   (B)    Violations of §
53.06 will result in a $50 fine to the person or persons that violate that
section.
(Ord. passed 3-2-2022)
