SNOWMOBILES
§ 71.01 OPERATING AT EXCESSIVE SPEED OR RECKLESSLY; OPERATING WITHOUT REQUIRED
MUFFLER.
   No person shall operate a snowmobile in the following manner:
   (A)   At a speed that is greater than is reasonable or prudent under the
circumstances;
   (B)   In any reckless way so as to endanger the person or property of
another; and
   (C)   Without a functioning muffler complying with SDCL § 32-20a.
(1992 Code, § 12-3-1) (Ord. 54, § 24-1, passed 2-17-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.02 IMPROPER USE ON CONTROLLED ACCESS HIGHWAY; OPERATION ON RAILROAD RIGHT-
OF-WAY.
   No snowmobile shall be operated upon or across a controlled access highway,
except that it may cross in the ditch of an underpass or on the extreme right
of an overpass. No snowmobile shall be operated, other than by a law
enforcement officer or a railroad employee in the lawful discharge of his or
her duties, upon any railroad right-of-way, except that it may be driven
directly across a railroad crossing after stopping and yielding the right-of-
way to approaching railroad traffic.
(1992 Code, § 12-3-2) (Ord. 54, § 24-2, passed 2-17-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.03 IMPROPER OPERATION ON OR ACROSS A ROADWAY.
   A snowmobile may be operated upon or across a roadway:
   (A)   To cross at right angles to the roadway only after stopping and
yielding the right-of-way to all approaching traffic and crossing as closely as
possible to an intersection or approach;
   (B)   When there is no ditch along either side of a roadway, then on the
shoulder or berm until there is a ditch on the right-hand side of the roadway
which can be traversed;
   (C)   When by reason of a bridge or culvert or other obstruction, it is
impossible to proceed, then only in the right lane of the roadway and for only
the distance as necessary to clear the obstruction;
   (D)   When permitted in writing by a law enforcement officer or a county
civil defense director as authorized under SDCL § 32-20a; and
   (E)   When snow has not been removed from a roadway which has been
obstructed and is not used by other types of motor vehicles.
(1992 Code, § 12-3-3) (Ord. 54, § 24-3, passed 2-17-1982)
§ 71.04 OPERATING WITHOUT LIGHTS WHEN DARK.
   Any snowmobile on a highway, operated during hours of darkness, shall
display a lighted head lamp and tail lamp in accordance with SDCL § 3220a as
may have been approved by the South Dakota Department of Public Safety at least
equivalent to that required for motorcycles.
(1992 Code, § 12-3-4) (Ord. 54, § 24-4, passed 2-17-1982)
MOTORCYCLES AND MOPEDS
§ 71.20 OPERATING WITHOUT DRIVER’S LICENSE.
   (A)   No person shall operate a motorcycle on the public streets or highways
without a motor vehicle driver's license or permit upon which a state testing
officer has certified that the person is qualified to operate the motorcycle.
   (B)   The South Dakota Department of Public Safety shall promulgate rules
and regulations to implement this section.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-1) (Ord. 52, § 22-1, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.21 HELMET REQUIRED UNDER 18 YEARS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person under 18 years of age to operate or ride
upon a motorcycle on the public streets or highways of the municipality, unless
the person wears a protective helmet of a type approved by the South Dakota
Department of Public Safety.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-2) (Ord. 52, § 22-2, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.22 PASSENGER SEAT.
   A person operating a motorcycle shall ride only upon the permanent and
regular seat attached thereto, and the operator shall not carry any other
person nor shall any other person ride on a motorcycle unless the motorcycle is
designed to carry more than 1 person, in which event a passenger may ride upon
the permanent and regular seat if designed for 2 persons, or upon another seat
firmly attached to the motorcycle at the rear or side of the operator.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-3) (Ord. 52, § 22-3, passed 3-24-1982)
§ 71.23 POSITION OF MOTORCYCLIST.
   A person shall ride upon a motorcycle only while sitting astride the
motorcycle and the seat thereof, facing forward.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-4) (Ord. 52, § 22-4, passed 3-24-1982)
§ 71.24 CARRYING OF PACKAGE WHICH DRIVER FROM KEEPING BOTH HANDS ON HANDLEBARS.
   No person shall operate a motorcycle while carrying any package, bundle or
other article which prevents him or her from keeping both hands on the
handlebars.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-5) (Ord. 52, § 22-5, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.25 RIDER INTERFERING WITH CONTROL OR VIEW OF OPERATOR.
   No operator shall carry any person, nor shall any person ride in a position
that will interfere with the operation or control of the motorcycle or the view
of the operator.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-6) (Ord. 52, § 22-6, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.26 CARRYING LOADED OR UNCASED GUN.
   It shall be unlawful for any person other than a law enforcement officer, or
conservation officer, to operate or ride on any motorcycle with any firearm in
his or her possession unless the firearm is completely unloaded and within a
carrying case which encloses the entire firearm.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-7) (Ord. 52, § 22-8, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.27 ATTACHMENT OF DRIVER OR CYCLE TO ANOTHER VEHICLE.
   No person riding upon a motorcycle shall attach himself or herself or the
motorcycle to any other vehicle on a roadway.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-8) (Ord. 52, § 22-7, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.28 OPERATING CYCLE IN MANNER DEPRIVING ANOTHER OF FULL USE OF DRIVING
LANE.
   All motorcycles are entitled to full use of a lane and no motor vehicle
shall be driven in such a manner as to deprive any motorcycle of the full use
of a lane. This section shall not apply to motorcycles operated 2 abreast in a
single lane.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-9) (Ord. 52, § 22-9, passed 3-24-1982)
§ 71.29 CYCLIST OVERTAKING AND PASSING MOTOR VEHICLE IN SAME LANE.
   The operator of a motorcycle shall not overtake and pass in the same lane
occupied by the vehicle being overtaken. This section shall not apply to
motorcycles being operated 2 abreast in the same lane, or a motorcycle and a
bicycle being operated 2 abreast in the same lane.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-10) (Ord. 52, § 22-10, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.30 OPERATING CYCLE BETWEEN ADJACENT LANES OF TRAFFIC.
   No person shall operate a motorcycle between adjacent lanes of traffic, or
between adjacent lines or rows of vehicles.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-11) (Ord. 52, § 22-11, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.31 OPERATING CYCLE MORE THAN 2 ABREAST IN SINGLE TRAFFIC LANES.
   Motorcycles shall not be operated more than 2 abreast in a single lane.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-12) (Ord. 52, § 22-12, passed 3-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 71.32 HELMETS AND EYE PROTECTION REQUIRED FOR PERSONS RIDING MOTORCYCLES,
MOTOR BIKES, AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or ride upon a
motorcycle on the public streets or alleys of the town, unless the person wears
a protective helmet and an eye protective device of a type approved by the
State Commissioner of Motor Vehicles. The eye protective device shall not be
required when the motorcycle is equipped with a windscreen.
   (B)   As used in this section, the term MOTORCYCLE includes motorcycles,
motor bikes, bicycles with motor attached and all motor operated vehicles of
the bicycle or tricycle type, whether the motive power is a part thereof or
attached thereto, and having a saddle or seat with the driver sitting astride
or upon it, or a platform on which the driver stands, but excluding a tractor.
This section shall not apply to persons riding within an enclosed cab.
(1992 Code, § 12-4-13) (Ord. 31, § 15-12, passed 10-1-1975) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Parallel and angle parking
   
72.02   Parking on highways prohibited in general
   
72.03   Mandatory clear, unobstructed view of vehicle parked in highway
   
72.04   Extended parking on Highway 16A (Winter Street) prohibited
   
72.05   Payment of fine upon violation of prohibited parking in Highway 16A
   
72.06   Immobilization of motor vehicle
   
72.07   Notice of vehicle immobilization
   
72.08   Release of immobilized vehicle
   
72.09   Post immobilization hearing
   
72.10   Towing and impoundment for failure to pay fines
   
72.11   Immobilization, towing and storage fees
   
72.12   Time period for enforcement
   
72.13   Hearing or trial
   
72.14   General parking prohibitions
   
72.15   No parking zones established; signs posted
   
72.16   Traffic fines and bond schedule
   
72.17   Designated parking spaces for commercial business employee parking
spaces
   
72.18   Commercial employees designated parking
§ 72.01 PARALLEL AND ANGLE PARKING.
   (A)   Except as otherwise specifically provided, every vehicle stopped or
parked upon a 2-way roadway shall be so stopped or parked with the right-hand
wheels parallel to, and within 12 inches of the right-hand curb or edge of the
roadway.
   (B)   Except when otherwise specifically provided, every vehicle stopped or
parked upon a 1-way roadway shall be so stopped or parked parallel to the curb
or edge of the roadway, in the direction of authorized traffic movement, with
its right-hand wheels within 12 inches of the right-hand curb or edge of the
roadway, or its left-hand wheels within 12 inches of the left-hand curb or edge
of the roadway.
   (C)   The Board of Trustees may, by ordinance, permit angle parking on any
roadway, except that angle parking shall not be permitted on any federal aid or
state highway unless the State Highway Commission has determined by resolution
or order entered in its minutes, that the roadway is of sufficient width to
permit angle parking without interfering with the free movement of traffic.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-1) (Ord. 31, § 15-60, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 72.02 PARKING ON HIGHWAYS PROHIBITED IN GENERAL.
   No person shall stop, park or leave standing any vehicle, whether attended
or unattended, upon the paved or improved or main traveled portion on any
highway, outside of a business or residence district, when it is practical to
stop, park or leave the vehicle standing off of the paved or improved or main
traveled portion of the highway.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-2) (Ord. 51, § 21-1, passed 18-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 72.03 MANDATORY CLEAR, UNOBSTRUCTED VIEW OF VEHICLE PARKED IN HIGHWAY.
   In no event shall any person park or leave standing any vehicle, whether
attended or unattended, upon any highway unless a clear or unobstructed width
of not less than 20 feet upon the main traveled portion of the highway opposite
the standing vehicle shall be left for free passage of other vehicles thereon,
nor unless a clear view of the vehicle may be obtained from a distance of 200
feet in each direction upon the highway.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-3) (Ord. 51, § 21-2, passed 18-24-1982) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 72.04 EXTENDED PARKING ON HIGHWAY 16A (WINTER STREET) PROHIBITED.
   There will be no parking on Winter Street between the hours of midnight and
6:00 a.m.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-4) (Ord.76, § a, passed 3-18-1987; Am. Ord. 76-88-b, passed
- - ; Am. Ord. 76-88-c, passed 6-15-1988; Am. Ord. 12-2-4, passed 4-18-2006;
Am. Ord. passed 8-3-2011; Am. Ord. passed 8-3-2011) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 72.05 PAYMENT OF FINE UPON VIOLATION OF PROHIBITED PARKING IN HIGHWAY 16A.
   The owner or operator of any vehicle found in violation may within 72 hours
of the time when the notice of violation was attached to the vehicle, pay to
the office of the town Finance Officer, as a penalty for and in full
satisfaction of the violation, the sum of $25. If the person fails to pay the
sum within the 72 hours, he or she may, within 2 weeks from the 72 hour period,
pay to the office as a penalty for and in full satisfaction of the violation,
the sum of $50. Upon failure of the person to pay either of the sums to the
office within the time periods indicated, and upon conviction of a violation of
this action, the person shall be fined not less than $75, or more than $100,
which shall be collected by the Magistrate Court in Rapid City, Pennington
County, South Dakota.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-5) (Ord. 76, § b, passed 3-18-1987; Am. Ord. passed 8-18-
1992)
§ 72.06 IMMOBILIZATION OF MOTOR VEHICLE.
   A motor vehicle, parked in violation of this section at any time, by or
under the direction of a law enforcement officer, may be immobilized in such a
manner as to prevent its operation, if there are 3 or more outstanding or
otherwise unsettled parking violation notices, or warrants issued for the
violations, pending against the owner of the motor vehicle.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-6) (Ord. 76, § c, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.07 NOTICE OF VEHICLE IMMOBILIZATION.
   Upon immobilization of the motor vehicle, the officer or employee shall
cause to be placed on the vehicle, in a conspicuous manner, notice sufficient
to warn any individual that the vehicle has been immobilized and that any
attempt to move the vehicle might result in damage to the vehicle. As soon as
practical, a notice shall be sent by first class mail informing the owner of
the immobilized vehicle of the nature and circumstances of the prior
outstanding or unsettled traffic violation notices or warrants for which, or on
account of which, the vehicle was immobilized.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-7) (Ord. 76, § d, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.08 RELEASE OF IMMOBILIZED VEHICLE.
   The owner of the immobilized vehicle, or other authorized person, shall be
permitted to secure release of the vehicle upon:
   (A)   Depositing the collateral required for his or her appearance in the
Magistrate Court to answer for each violation; and
   (B)   Depositing the amount of the fine or penalty for each violation for
which there is an outstanding or otherwise unsettled parking violation notice
or warrant.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-8) (Ord. 76, § e, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.09 POST IMMOBILIZATION HEARING.
   (A)   The owner of an immobilized vehicle, or other authorized person, shall
have the right to a past-immobilization hearing to determine the validity of
the immobilization, towing and any towing or storage charges.
   (B)   The hearing must be requested within 15 days after the vehicle is
immobilized and shall be conducted by the Clerk of Courts for the Magistrate
Court, Seventh Judicial Circuit, Pennington County, South Dakota.
   (C)   The post immobilization hearing will not be determinative of or
adjudicate any citation issued relative to any immobilized vehicle.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-9) (Ord. 76, § e, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.10 TOWING AND IMPOUNDMENT FOR FAILURE TO PAY FINES.
   The immobilizing device or mechanism shall remain in place for 48 hours
unless the owner has complied within §§
72.08 and
72.09 of this chapter. If the compliance has not occurred within 48 hours, the
vehicle shall be towed or impounded. Towing and storage fees shall be paid,
along with fees specified before the owner of the vehicle, or authorized person
shall be permitted to repossess or secure the release of the vehicle.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-10) (Ord. 76, § f, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.11 IMMOBILIZATION, TOWING AND STORAGE FEES.
   The owner of an immobilized vehicle shall be subject to a fee of $35 for the
immobilization. The owner of an immobilized vehicle which was impounded shall
be subject to a total fee of $80 plus a fee for storage.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-11) (Ord. 76, § g, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.12 TIME PERIOD FOR ENFORCEMENT.
   The town law enforcement shall have authority for implementing the parking
enforcement provisions of this section from May 1 through September 30 of each
calendar year.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-12) (Ord. 76, § h, passed 3-18-1987; Am. Ord. 76-88-a,
passed 2-17-1988; Am. Ord. 12-2-12, passed 11-19-2003)
§ 72.13 HEARING OR TRIAL.
   Nothing in this section shall be construed to deprive any person of the
constitutional right to a hearing or trial as to the violations charged.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-13) (Ord. 76, § h, passed 3-18-1987)
§ 72.14 GENERAL PARKING PROHIBITIONS.
   The operator of a vehicle shall not stop, stand or park the vehicle in any
of the following places, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other
traffic or in compliance with the directions of a police officer, traffic
control sign or signal:
   (A)   Within an intersection;
   (B)   Within 15 feet of the driveway entrance to a fire station;
   (C)   In front of a private driveway;
   (D)   On a sidewalk;
   (E)   Contrary to signs designating parking or prohibitions; and
   (F)   Within a yellow zone.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-14) (Ord. 45, § 28-125, passed 4-18-1979; Am. Ord. passed 4-
3-2013)
§ 72.15 NO PARKING ZONES ESTABLISHED; SIGNS POSTED.
   The Town of Keystone, with respect to streets and alleys under its
jurisdiction, may place signs prohibiting, restricting or limiting the
stopping, standing or parking of vehicles on any street or alley, where, in the
opinion of the Board of Trustees, as evidenced by resolution, entered into in
its minutes, stopping, standing or parking is not in the best interest of the
public and/or the municipality. The signs shall be official signs and no person
shall stop, stand or park any vehicle in violation of the restrictions stated
on the signs.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-15) (Ord. 40, passed 4-19-1978)
§ 72.16 TRAFFIC FINES AND BOND SCHEDULE.
   Where the violation charged for any traffic offense is comparable to the
same charge for a violation of a state statute the Magistrate may adopt for the
purposes of determining fines and bonds, the fine and bond schedule promulgated
pursuant to the order of the presiding Circuit Court Judge for the Seventh
Judicial District of South Dakota.
(1992 Code, § 12-2-16) (Ord. 55, 25-1, passed 3-17-1982)
§ 72.17 DESIGNATED PARKING SPACES FOR COMMERCIAL BUSINESS EMPLOYEE PARKING
SPACES.
   The Town Board of Trustees is authorized to designate parking spaces for any
commercial business employees along Swanzey Street.
   (A)   Lines shall be painted upon the curb adjacent to each commercial
business employee parking space and upon the street, designating the parking
space for each vehicle to park within the lines. It is unlawful to park any
vehicle across any such line, or to park a vehicle in such a position that it
shall not be entirely within the space designated by the lines.
   (B)   No person other than a commercial business employee may park in the
designated space between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. Any person who
parks a vehicle found in violation of this section shall, within 72 hours from
the time when the notice of violation was attached to the vehicle, pay the
Finance Office, as a penalty for and in full satisfaction of the violation in
accordance with §
72.05.
   (C)   (1)   No person shall park or otherwise cause a vehicle to occupy a
designated employee space without prominently displaying a valid parking permit
issued by the city, upon application for that purpose. Parking permits shall be
valid through the date shown on the face of the permit or until the holder of
the permit no longer meets the eligibility requirements determined by the city.
      (2)   No person shall display or allow to be displayed a permit unless
said permit is issued to that person. No person shall disfigure, display,
obscure, loan, give or otherwise allow any other person to use a permit issued
to them. Any vehicle parked in an employee designated space without a permit so
displayed will be deemed to be in violation of this chapter.
      (3)   Emergency, government and public utility vehicles engaged in
official business shall be exempt from permit requirements. The issuance of an
employee permit is applicable only to those spaces so designated and the
issuance of said permit does not guarantee the availability of a parking space.
      (4)   For the purpose of this section, the following definition shall
apply unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
         PROMINENTLY DISPLAYED.  
            1.   For cars, trucks and other enclosed vehicles: to be suspended
from the rear view mirror or visor so as to face toward the front of the
vehicle and visible from the exterior of the vehicle.
            2.   For motorcycles: To be attached to the handlebar in such a
manner as to be visible from the front of the vehicle.
   (D)   Any person who operates a vehicle found in violation of this section
shall, within 72 hours from the time when the notice of violation was attached
to the vehicle, pay the Finance Office, as a penalty for and in full
satisfaction of the violation in accordance with §
72.05.
(Ord. passed 5-19-2010)
§ 72.18 COMMERCIAL EMPLOYEES DESIGNATED PARKING.
   All commercial employees working in the town shall park within the
designated employee parking area between 6:00 a.m. and 11:00 p.m.
(Ord. passed 3-15-2017)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 ANIMAL WASTE; RESPONSIBILITY.
   (A)   No person shall create or maintain any condition or equipment or keep
any animal, fowl, pet or insect under his or her jurisdiction in which causes
the transmission of diseases from animals or insects to humans.
   (B)   No owner, keeper, caretaker or attendant of an animal shall permit
such animal to defecate on public or private property other than his or her
own. If the animal does defecate upon public or private property, the owner,
keeper, caretaker or attendant must immediately and thoroughly clean the fecal
matter from the property.
   (C)   Anyone walking an animal on public or private property other than his
or her own must carry with him or her means of cleaning up any fecal matter
left by the animal. Animals used in parades or involved in law enforcement are
exempt from this section.
   (D)   For purposes of this chapter, the term ANIMAL shall include any
mammal, bird, reptile, amphibian, or fish, except humans.
(Ord. 2-1-12, passed 2-21-2007; Am. Ord. passed 7-18-2012) Penalty, see §
90.99
DOGS AND OTHER ANIMALS
§ 90.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL. Shall include any mammal, bird, reptile, amphibian, or fish, except
humans.
   AT-LARGE ANIMAL. Any animal shall be deemed to be AT-LARGE when he or she is
off the property of his or her owner and not under control of a competent
person.
   OWNER. Any person, group of persons or corporation owning, keeping or
harboring a dog or other animal.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-1) (Ord. 44, § 6-1, passed 1-26-1990; Am. Ord. passed 7-18-
2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-29-3, 9-29-12
§ 90.16 ANIMALS TO BE KEPT UNDER RESTRAINT.
   The owner or custodian of any animal shall not permit the animal to be at-
large off the premises or property of the owner or custodian unless under the
control of a competent person by means of a leash or securely confined within a
vehicle.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-2) (Ord. 44, § 6-2, passed 1-26-1990; Am. Ord. passed 7-18-
2012)
§ 90.17 NUISANCE DOGS NOT PERMITTED IN TOWN LIMITS.
   The owner shall keep his or her dog under restraint at all times and shall
not permit the dog to be at- large off the premises or property of the owner,
unless under the control of a competent person. It shall be unlawful for any
dog owner to keep, or have within the town limits, a dog that habitually or
repeatedly chases, snaps at or attacks livestock, poultry, pedestrians,
bicyclists or vehicles, or turns over garbage pails, damages gardens, flowers,
vegetables or conducts itself as to be a public nuisance.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-4) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0101, passed 2-18-1987) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.18 IMPOUNDMENT AND DISPOSITION OF ANIMALS.
   All animals found running-at-large shall be taken up by the animal warden or
law enforcement officer, at his or her discretion, and impounded in the county
animal shelter. Animals impounded and not claimed by their owners at the
expiration of 3 days may be destroyed. When animals are found running- at-
large, and their ownership is known to the animal warden or law enforcement
officer, the animals need not be impounded, but the animal warden or law
enforcement officer may at his or her discretion, cite the owners of the
animals to appear in court to answer charges of violations of this section.
Should the animal warden or law enforcement officer know the identity of the
owner of any animal he or she has caused to be impounded, he or she may notify
the owner and inform him or her of the conditions whereby he or she may regain
possession of the animal.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-5) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0102, passed 2-18-1987; Am. Ord. passed 7-
18-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-29-12, 9-29-3
§ 90.19 INVESTIGATION AND RIGHT OF ENTRY.
   For the purpose of discharging the duties imposed by this subchapter and to
enforce its provisions, the animal warden or any law enforcement officer is
authorized and empowered to follow and enter upon any enclosure or lot within
the limits of the town to apprehend any animal which he or she has observed to
be running-at-large.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-6) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0103, passed 2-18-1987; Am. Ord. passed 7-
18-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-29-12, 9-29-3
§ 90.20 RABIES CONTROL, BITING ANIMALS AND QUARANTINES.
   Every animal which bites a person shall be promptly reported to the animal
warden, and shall there- upon be securely quarantined for a period of not less
than 10 days. The quarantine may be at the shelter designated as the county
animal shelter, or at the owners' option, in a veterinary hospital within
Pennington County. The expenses of the quarantine shall be paid by the owner of
the dog. Every owner having knowledge that his or her animal has bitten, or is
suspected of biting a human being, shall forthwith report the same to the
county animal control officer for disposition of the animal.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-7) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0104, passed 2-18-1987)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-29-12, 9-29-3, 9-34-1
§ 90.21 CONFINEMENT OF BITING DOGS.
   (A)   Any dog which has ever bitten any person so as to break the skin, to
the knowledge of the person owning or taking care of the dog, must keep the dog
in a secure enclosure, or the dog must be accompanied by a person who, by means
of a leash, has the dog under control at all times.
   (B)   If this condition is violated, in addition to any other penalty, the
dog shall be taken by the county animal control officer and destroyed.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-8) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0105, passed 2-18-1987) Penalty, see §
90.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-29-12, 9-29-13, 9-29-3
§ 90.22 INTERFERENCE WITH ANIMAL WARDEN PROHIBITED.
   No person shall interfere with, or hinder any official in the performance of
any duty of his or her office, or seek to release any animal in custody.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-9) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0106, passed 2-18-1987) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.23 PROVISIONS OF COUNTY ORDINANCE TO PREVAIL.
   (A)   The foregoing Board of Trustees does not preclude any of the
provisions of animal control set forward in the Pennington County Animal
Control Ordinance.
   (B)   Therefore, the provisions of the Pennington County Ordinance will
apply in any situations not directly addressed.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-11) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0108, passed 2-18-1987)
ANIMAL DRAWN CONVEYANCES
§ 90.40 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AMUSEMENT or FEE. Any animal drawn conveyance which solicits monies from the
passengers therein, or which conveyance is used in the promotion of any
business.
   ANIMAL DRAWN CONVEYANCE. Any wagon, stagecoach or buggy within which people
are carried and which is drawn by any animal, including, but not limited to,
horses, mules, donkeys, buffalo and oxen.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-1) (Ord. 21, § 18-1, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 90.41 ISSUANCE OF LICENSE AND INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS.
   No person shall operate any animal drawn conveyance for amusement or fee
within the boundaries of the municipality of Town of Keystone, without having
first obtained a license therefor from the Town of Keystone, insuring the
owner, owner's employees and the Town of Keystone, against liability for
personal injury, death or property damage arising out of the ownership,
occupancy or use of the animal drawn conveyance upon the public right-of-way.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-2) (Ord. 21, § 18-2, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. 65, passed 5-
9-1985) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.42 LICENSE FEE.
   The fee for obtaining a license for the purpose of operating an animal drawn
conveyance for amusement or fee shall be the sum of $75 to be renewed annually,
and will be on file and available for inspection during the regular business
hours with the Finance Officer, Town Hall, Town of Keystone, South Dakota.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-3) (Ord. 31, § 18-3, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. 41, passed 6-
21-1978: Am. Ord. 65, passed 5-9-1985)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 9-34-1, 9-34-10, 9-34-13
§ 90.43 PREMISES AND LITTER.
   Any person operating an animal drawn conveyance for amusement or fee shall
operate from a fixed place of business which shall be designated on the
license, and shall be responsible for keeping the area clean and free of all
litter and manure, and shall also be responsible for keeping the route traveled
clean and free of any litter and manure caused by the operation.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-4) (Ord. 31, § 18-4, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 90.44 SALES TAX APPLICABLE.
   The owner or operator for fee of any animal drawn conveyance, within the
municipal boundaries of the Town of Keystone, shall be responsible for
complying with the municipal 2% sales tax ordinance, and shall also be subject
to all town and state provisions applicable to the driver of any vehicle being
maintained on a public street or highway.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-5) (Ord. 31, § 18-5, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 90.45 SANITARY BAGS MANDATORY.
   Any person operating an animal drawn conveyance or animals for hire for
amusement or fee, shall place bags or other apparatuses around the animals to
prevent manure droppings on town properties and rights-of-way.
(1992 Code, § 2-2-7) (Ord. 65A, passed 5-5-1986)
§ 90.98 ENFORCEMENT.
   The animal control or law enforcement officer has discretion for any
violation under this entire chapter.
(Ord. passed 4-1-2014)
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)    Violation of any part of§ 90.01(B) is punishable by a fine of not
less than $25 nor more than $200.
(Ord. 2-1-12, passed 2-21-2007)
   (C)   Violation of §§
90.15 and
90.16 shall result in a fine of not less than $5, nor more than $100.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-3) (Ord. 44, § 6-2, passed 1-26-1990)
   (D)   Any person, firm or corporation violating §§
90.17 through
90.23, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punishable by a fine of not less
than $25 nor more than $100, or by confinement not to exceed 30 days in the
county jail or both the fine and imprisonment.
(1992 Code, § 2-1-10) (Ord. 44A, § 1.0107, passed 2-18-1987)
CHAPTER 91: ABANDONED VEHICLES
Section
   
91.01   Definitions
   
91.02   Storing, parking or leaving dismantled or other motor vehicles declared
nuisance; with exception
   
91.03   Fences required
   
91.04   Advertisement on fences
   
91.05   Storing, parking or leaving dismantled or other motor vehicles on
public property prohibited
   
91.06   Removal of abandoned or junked vehicles
   
91.07   Notice to owner
   
91.08   Duty of private owners
   
91.09   Notice to remove abandoned or junked vehicle
   
91.10   Racing or antique vehicles
 
   
91.99   Penalty
§ 91.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle which is left unattended on any
public street or alley, in any public parking lot or in any other public place
for more than 24 consecutive hours.
   JUNK MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle which does not have lawfully affixed
thereto unexpired license plates or which is wrecked, dismantled, partially
dismantled, inoperable or discarded.
   MOTOR VEHICLE. Any self-propelled vehicle including but not limited to
automobiles, motorcycles, motor scooters, trucks, tractors, go-carts, golf
carts and campers.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-1) (Ord. 81, § 1, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.02 STORING, PARKING OR LEAVING DISMANTLED OR OTHER MOTOR VEHICLES DECLARED
NUISANCE; WITH EXCEPTION.
   (A)   The presence of an abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, junk
or partially dismantled motor vehicle or parts thereof, on private or public
property, is hereby declared a public nuisance.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to any motor vehicle enclosed within a
building on private property or to any motor vehicle held in connection with a
business enterprise, properly operated or any motor vehicle in operable
condition specifically adapted or designed for operation on drag strips or
raceways, which vehicle remains on private property, or any motor vehicle
retained on private property by the owner for antique collection purposes and
covered with an appropriate cover to screen it from view.
   (C)   This section also does not apply to unlicensed vehicles held in
connection with the business enterprise including used auto parts, so long as
the business stores the vehicles in an enclosed fenced area.
   (D)   This section also applies to any type of equipment operated by a motor
vehicle including, but not limited to, boats and off highway equipment.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-2) (Ord. 81, § 2, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.03 FENCES REQUIRED.
   Any business storing vehicles or used auto parts shall be entirely enclosed
by a fence 8 feet in height which shall be kept neatly painted in natural earth
colors and in good repair at all times, and which will be constructed of a
minimum of 1 inch dimension rough or finished lumber or corrugated iron, so as
to exclude the yard from public view. A period of 60 days from the date of the
passage of this chapter is allowed the operators of the yards to construct the
fence or fences required by this chapter.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-3) (Ord. 81, § 2a, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.04 ADVERTISEMENT ON FENCES.
   (A)   The fence enclosing the business shall not be used for bill postings
or other advertising purposes, except that a space not larger than 8 by 12 feet
may be used for the advertisement of the business of the owner thereof. Where
the yard fronts on more than 1 street, the use of space for advertising herein
permitted shall extend to each street on which the yard abuts.
   (B)   The contents are not to extend about the height of the fence. Any
person or business storing motor vehicles and used auto parts shall not place
or deposit the contents to a height greater than the height of the fence
surrounding it.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-4) (Ord. 81, § 2b,c passed 4-18-1990) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.05 STORING, PARKING OR LEAVING DISMANTLED OR OTHER MOTOR VEHICLES ON
PUBLIC PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   No person shall park, store, leave or permit the parking, storing or leaving
of any abandoned or junk motor vehicle of any kind, whether attended or not,
upon any public property within the town.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-5) (Ord. 81, §3, passed 4-18-1990) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.06 REMOVAL OF ABANDONED OR JUNKED VEHICLES.
   (A)   Whenever any police officer finds an abandoned motor vehicle or junk
motor vehicle on public property, he or she shall place written notice on the
vehicle that it will be removed at the owner's expense, or a fine of $25 will
be issued for each continuous 24 hours period.
   (B)   After the expiration of the 24 hour period, the vehicle may be removed
by the removal agency to a garage or place of safety. Nothing in this chapter
precludes the Police Department from immediately removing a motor vehicle which
causes an obstruction or hazard to traffic.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-6) (Ord. 81, § 4, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.07 NOTICE TO OWNER.
   It shall be the duty of the Police Department to notify, by certified mail
or in person, the registered owner, and if encumbered, the lien holder, of the
removal, storage and present location of any motor vehicle removed under the
provisions of this chapter, and that the vehicle can be recovered by payment to
the removal agency.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-7) (Ord. 81, § 5, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.08 DUTY OF PRIVATE OWNERS.
   No person owning, in charge of, or in control of any real property within
the Town of Keystone, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise,
shall allow any abandoned or junk motor vehicle of any kind to remain on the
property longer than 30 days.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-8) (Ord. 81, § 6, passed 4-18-1990) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.09 NOTICE TO REMOVE ABANDONED OR JUNKED VEHICLE.
   Whenever it comes to the attention of the Police Department by way of 2 or
more complaints in writing from 2 adult residents of the Town of Keystone, who
do not reside at the same residence, that any person has an abandoned or junk
motor vehicle on his or her property, a notice in writing from the law
enforcement department shall be served by certified mail or personal service
upon the person ordering the removal of the motor vehicle in the time specified
in this section. The notice shall contain the request for removal within 30
days after the mailing of or service of the notice, and the notice shall advise
that failure to comply with the notice to remove shall be a violation of this
section.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-9) (Ord. 81, § 7, passed 4-18-1990)
§ 91.10 RACING OR ANTIQUE VEHICLES.
   No owner or occupant of private property shall have an uncovered motor
vehicle in operating condition specifically adapted or designed for operation
on drag strips or raceways, or an uncovered motor vehicle retained on private
property for antique collection purposes.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-10) (Ord. 81, § 8, passed 4-18-1990) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction shall be subject to a penalty not to
exceed 30 days imprisonment, a fine of $100 or both.
(1992 Code, § 12-5-11) (Ord. 81, § 9, passed 4-18-1990)
CHAPTER 92: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
Section
   
92.01   Street names
   
92.02   Permit and deposit for street excavations
   
92.03   Restoring surface materials
   
92.04   Returning deposit
   
92.05   Responsibility for lights and guards around and damages resulting from
street excavations
   
92.06   Board permission for parades or public gatherings on streets or
sidewalks
   
92.07   Removal of snow and ice from sidewalks
   
92.08   Cleaning of sidewalks and alleys
   
92.09   Regulating signs, awnings, canopies and marquees
   
92.10   Encroachments prohibited

§ 92.01 STREET NAMES.
   The names of the streets in the town are hereby fixed and adopted in
accordance with and as shown by the map of the town on file in the office of
the Finance Officer.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-1) (Ord. 31, § 16-1, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 92.02 PERMIT AND DEPOSIT FOR STREET EXCAVATIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to dig any hole or make any
excavation in any public street or alley in the town, unless the person first
secures a permit to do so.
   (B)   The Finance Officer shall issue a permit to any person requesting the
same upon deposit with the Finance Officer of the sum as the Finance Officer
determines to be sufficient as a guarantee that any hole or excavation placed
in any public street or alley by the applicant shall be properly filled and
tamped so as to avoid settlement of fill material at a later time.
   (C)   In the event any dispute arises between the applicant and the Finance
Officer as to the amount of the deposit, the matter shall be referred to the
Board of Trustees, and its decision shall be final.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-2) (Ord. 31, § 16-2.1, passed 10-1-1975) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.03 RESTORING SURFACE MATERIALS.
   The surface material shall be restored as was originally present when the
excavations occurred, and the Finance Officer shall show on the excavation
permit the type of surface material to be used.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-3) (Ord. 31, § 16-2.2, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 92.04 RETURNING DEPOSIT.
   The Finance Officer shall return a deposit made under §
92.02, 12 months after any hole or excavation dug in the public streets or
alleys has been filled or upon advice from the Engineer or his or her
representative that the hole or excavation has been properly filled and tamped
so as to avoid settlement of fill material at a later time. In the event the
town must, within 12 months, cause the hole or excavation to be filled or
repaired, the deposit shall be forfeited.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-4) (Ord. 31, § 16-2.3, passed 10-1-1975; Am. Ord. 10-1-4A,
passed 1-20-1999)
§ 92.05 RESPONSIBILITY FOR LIGHTS AND GUARDS AROUND AND DAMAGES RESULTING FROM
STREET EXCAVATIONS.
   The person holding a permit shall be responsible for lights and guards
around the street opening and for all damages claimed by, or accruing to,
persons or property as a result of the street opening.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-5) (Ord. 31, § 16-3, passed 10-1-1975)
§ 92.06 BOARD PERMISSION FOR PARADES OR PUBLIC GATHERINGS ON STREETS OR
SIDEWALKS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person or persons, organizations, clubs or
institutions to hold or conduct any parade, meeting or public gathering on the
streets or sidewalks of the town, without first obtaining permission so to do
from the Board of Trustees.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-6) (Ord. 31, § 16-4, passed 10-1-1975) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.07 REMOVAL OF SNOW AND ICE FROM SIDEWALKS.
   The owner or occupant of any lot or parcel of land in the town abutting upon
any sidewalk shall, within 12 hours after any fall of snow upon the sidewalk,
or within 12 hours after snow or ice had, from any cause, collected upon the
sidewalk, remove the same from so much of the sidewalk as adjoins his or her
premises. If any occupant or owner shall fail to remove snow or ice within the
specified 12 hours, he or she shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. In case
of vacant lots, the work shall be ordered 1 by the Chief of Police and
certified against the lot with the taxes thereon.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-7) (Ord. 31, § 16-5, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-30-5
§ 92.08 CLEANING OF SIDEWALKS AND ALLEYS.
   (A)   The occupant or owner of any lot or parcel of land in the town
abutting on any alley or sidewalk shall keep the sidewalk and the gutter in
front of the same, and the alley to the center thereof, free from all filth,
unwholesome substance or matter, manure, straw, brush or rubbish of any sort.
   (B)   If any occupant or owner shall fail to remove any filth, unwholesome
substance or matter, manure, straw, brush or rubbish of any sort for more than
24 hours after receiving notice so to do from the Chief of Police, he or she
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-8) (Ord. 31, § 16-6, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-30-2
§ 92.09 REGULATING SIGNS, AWNINGS, CANOPIES AND MARQUEES.
   (A)   No signs, awnings, canopies, marquees or other encroachments of
whatever nature will be permitted to exist in or overhang into the dedicated
street from property line to property line, or on any street or federal
highway, except as described below.
   (B)   On Winter Street from the intersection with Reed Street to
approximately 300 feet north of Mitchell Street, signs, awnings, canopies and
marquees, when attached to buildings or supports located on private property,
may overhang to within 3 feet of the face of the curb provided there is no
obstruction or interference with official traffic control devices.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-9) (Ord. 31, § 16-7, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-30-2
§ 92.10 ENCROACHMENTS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place any goods, wares or merchandise
for exhibition or sale upon any public street, alley, sidewalk or any public
grounds in the town, or place or cause to be placed thereon any goods, wares,
merchandise, bottles, cans, cases, packages, barrels or other containers, at
any time for exhibition, sale or any other purpose, or place or cause to be
placed thereon, any advertising sign, bicycle rack, popcorn stand or rack, or
any other movable property, article or material which in any manner obstructs
or interferes with the free use of the public street, road, alley, sidewalk or
public ground.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-10) (Ord. 42, passed 6-21-1978) Penalty, see §
92.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL Ch. 9-30
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   In addition to the abatement remedies prescribed in this section, any
person convicted of being in violation of §§
92.01 through
92.09 of this chapter shall be punished by a fine of not less than $1 nor more
than $100, or imprisonment in jail not longer than 30 days, or both the fine
and imprisonment.
(1992 Code, § 10-1-9) (Ord. 31, § 16-7, passed 10-1-1975)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-30-2
CHAPTER 93: FIREWORKS
Section
   
93.01   Definition
   
93.02   Fireworks prohibited within town limits; with exception
   
93.03   Permit required for public fireworks display
§ 93.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition shall apply unless
the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   FIREWORKS. Pyrotechnics or fireworks containing phosphorus, sulfocyanate,
mercury, chlorate of potash and sulfur and sulfur or chlorate of potash and
sugar, and the following names of fireworks:
      (1)   Firecrackers;
      (2)   Flash crackers or salutes;
      (3)   Blank cartridges;
      (4)   Cherry bombs;
      (5)   Sky rockets (including all devices which rise in the air during
discharge);
      (6)   Roman candles (including all devices discharging balls of fire into
the air);
      (7)   Chasers (including all devices which dart or travel above the
surface of the ground during discharge);
      (8)   Snakes, boa constrictors and snake nests containing bichloride or
mercury;
      (9)   All articles for pyrotechnic display which contain gun powder;
      (10)   Articles commonly known as son-of-a-gun;
      (11)   Devil on the rock;
      (12)   Cricket sticks;
      (13)   Automatic torpedoes which contain arsenic;
      (14)   Explosives known as devil-on-the-walk;
      (15)   Other articles of similar character which explode through the
means of friction or by fuse; and
      (16)   All other fireworks, except cap pistol paper caps, containing not
more than 25/100 of a grain of explosive compound to each paper cap.
(1992 Code, § 9-1-1) (Ord. 48, § c, passed 11-14-1979)
§ 93.02 FIREWORKS PROHIBITED WITHIN TOWN LIMITS; WITH EXCEPTION.
   No person shall discharge or have in his or her possession, or shall
manufacture, sell, give away or transport any fireworks within the town or
within 1 mile of its limits; provided, however, that nothing in this chapter
shall be held to apply to the following:
   (A)   The possession or use of signaling devices by railways or public
officials in the course of his or her duties;
   (B)   Any person giving a display of fireworks in any public park, or upon
any other place in the town under and in accordance with a permit issued;
   (C)   The possession, sale or use of flashlight composition by
photographers, dealers in photographic supplies, or by any other person using
the flashlight composition for the purpose of taking pictures;
   (D)   The sale or use of blank cartridges for ceremonial purposes, athletic,
theatrical or sporting events, though a permit to use the same shall be
obtained from the Board of Trustees prior to its use;
   (E)   The discharge or firing of target pistols, guns or rifles in any gun
club, at any duly authorized outdoor target range; and
   (F)   Toy pistol paper caps containing not more than 25/100 grain explosive
compound to each paper cap.
(1992 Code, § 9-1-2) (Ord. 48, § c, passed 11-14-1979) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 34-37-4, 34-37-16.1, 34-35-5, 9-29-3
§ 93.03 PERMIT REQUIRED FOR PUBLIC FIREWORKS DISPLAY.
   (A)   Any person desiring to give a display of fireworks in any public park
or in any open place within the town, shall obtain therefor, a written permit
from the Board of Trustees.
   (B)   A similar permit shall be required to be obtained by any person
seeking to establish or maintain any indoor or outdoor target range within the
town.
(1992 Code, § 9-1-3) (Ord. 48, § b, passed 11-14-1979)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL §§ 34-37-16.1, 34-37-4, 34-37-10
CHAPTER 94: TOWN CEMETERY
Section
   
94.01   Name
   
94.02   Powers and authority
   
94.03   Budget
   
94.04   Sale of lots
   
94.05   Graves and monuments
§ 94.01 NAME.
   The Town Cemetery shall be known as the Mountain View Cemetery, Keystone,
South Dakota.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2006)
§ 94.02 POWERS AND AUTHORITY.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees shall establish rates for the sale of cemetery
lots within the Mountain View Cemetery and shall periodically make adjustment
of the sale prices. The Town Finance Officer shall have the power to receive,
receipt and deposit moneys into the general fund to provide for the operations
and maintenance of the cemetery.
   (B)   A Cemetery Advisory Committee shall be appointed by the Town Board and
shall have 3 to 5 members. The Cemetery Advisory Committee has the authority to
make a recommendation to the Keystone Board of Trustees on whether a
prospective purchaser of a burial plot may purchase the same at the discounted
price set forth in §
94.04. The ultimate decision shall be rendered by the Keystone Board of
Trustees. The Cemetery Advisory Committee shall meet a minimum of 1 day per
year.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2006; Ord. passed 10-21-2020)
§ 94.03 BUDGET.
   The town shall on or before the first day of August of each year, submit a
proposed budget for the ensuing year showing the anticipated receipts from sale
of lots if any, and the projected anticipated maintenance expense of the
cemetery.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2006)
§ 94.04 SALE OF LOTS.
   (A)   Prospective purchasers of burial plots in the Mountain View Cemetery
who can provide competent evidence and factually establish that they are a
lineal descendant or sibling of a person buried in the Mountain View Cemetery;
or who currently resides within a 30 mile radius of the Town of Keystone
municipal limits; or if extraordinary and special circumstances are established
and approved by the Keystone Board of Trustees, may purchase a burial plot by
paying the required fee of $300 to the Town of Keystone.
   (B)   Any prospective purchaser, who fails to meet the criteria to purchase
a burial plot at the discounted fee set forth in § 94.04(A), must petition the
Cemetery Advisory Committee, subject to the final approval from the Keystone
Board of Trustees, and upon the Keystone Board of Trustees approval, may
purchase a burial plot by paying the required fee $1,500 to the Town of
Keystone.
   (C)   Upon full payment of the required fees the Town Finance Officer shall
issue to the purchaser an official deed for the burial plot. Re-sale of burial
plots, unless to immediate family, is strictly prohibited. The town does not
buy back burial plots. Burial plots may be donated back to the town.
   (D)   In addition to the power granted to the Town of Keystone in SDCL §§ 9-
32-21 and 47-29-9, relating to the reselling of cemetery lots, the Town of
Keystone shall have the right to discontinue all rights granted to a purchaser
for any burial plot after a period of 30 years from the date of sale thereof,
should the Board of Trustees, upon investigation, determine that the purchaser
or owner thereof has not used the lot, or any part thereof, that the owner is
deceased and that the burial plot will not likely be used as a burial place for
the owner or purchaser or any lineal descendant or siblings.
   (E)   In the event that any such burial plot is reclaimed, inquiry shall be
made to ascertain the names and addresses of the heirs or any of them, which
can be obtained by the making of a reasonable inquiry and investigation, and
notice shall be given to the heirs by mail, of the intention of the Town of
Keystone to reclaim the property. Notice and transfer shall be in accordance
with South Dakota law.
   (F)    In the event no heir of a deceased owner is located, notice of the
reclaiming of the burial plot and the deposit of the money shall be published
once a week for 3 successive weeks in the official newspaper for the Town of
Keystone. It is the responsibility of the owner, purchaser or any member of
their family to maintain updated contact information with the town. Any person
who purchases any burial plot shall, by that purchase be deemed to have agreed,
on behalf of himself or herself and his or her heirs and assigns, to hold the
Town of Keystone harmless for any damages resulting from an inadvertent burial
on the wrong burial plot, or for any damage to any stone, marker or other
improvement placed on the burial plot so purchased.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2006; Ord. passed 10-21-2020)
§ 94.05 GRAVES AND MONUMENTS.
   (A)   No interment shall be made of 2 or more bodies in 1 grave, unless the
case is a cremation then 2 cremations can be in 1 grave. It is the family's
and/or deed holder's responsibility to keep track of where each cremation is
located within the burial plot to avoid disturbing previous burials.
   (B)   Monuments and markers are not the Town of Keystone property.
Maintenance and vandalism are the responsibility of the deed holder or personal
representative of the estate.
   (C)   No disinterment in a burial plot or grave space will be permitted
without documentation, as prescribed by South Dakota Law, in writing by the
surviving husband, wife or next of kin of the person whose body is to be
disinterred, and written permit, order for the disinterment from the owner of
the lot, or his or her lawful representative.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2006; Ord. passed 10-21-2020)
CHAPTER 95: BURNING OF SLASH PILES
Section
   
95.01   Definitions
   
95.02   Materials allowed in piles
   
95.03   Permit required before burning slash pile
   
95.04   Regulations governing slash piles
 
   
95.99   Penalty
§ 95.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   LARGER SLASH PILES. After the effective date of this chapter a special
permit can be obtained for slash piles that exceed the height and diameter
limitations described below so long as the same is approved by the Battle Creek
Fire Department.
   SLASH. The accumulation of vegetative materials such as tops, limbs,
branches, brush, and miscellaneous residue resulting from forest management
activities such as thinning, pruning, timber harvesting, and wildfire hazard
mitigation.
   SMALL SLASH PILE. A small slash pile is a brush pile constructed by hand, no
larger than 5 feet in height and 6 foot in diameter.
(Ord. passed 11-15-2023)
§ 95.02 MATERIALS ALLOWED IN PILES.
   Materials allowed in slash piles include limbs, tree tops, brush, grass and
miscellaneous materials recently cut in the area.
§ 95.03 PERMIT REQUIRED BEFORE BURNING SLASH PILE.
   (A)   The burning of a slash pile within the jurisdiction of the Town of
Keystone by a person or a group of persons is prohibited unless a permit to do
so is first obtained from the Battle Creek Fire Department upon such forms as
are provided from the Battle Creek Fire Department.
   (B)   Every applicant for a permit shall provide verification that the
applicant has viewed the slash pile burning instruction video referenced in the
application before the application will be approved.
   (C)   Every applicant shall sign a waiver of liability and indemnity
agreement holding the Town of Keystone and the Battle Creek Fire Department
harmless from any liability resulting from the intentional or negligent act of
the applicant and the person the applicant has designated as the person whom
will be involved in the burning process.
(Ord. passed 11-15-2023)
§ 95.04 REGULATIONS GOVERNING SLASH PILES.
   (A)   Burning of a slash pile is not permitted during periods of high winds,
low humidity or drying conditions are forecasted to develop after starting.
Permits are only valid when there is continuous snow cover with the depth of
snow being at least 2 inches and the fire index danger category is moderate or
low. Fire danger in the high, very high, and extreme categories shall suspend
the permit until the fire index danger returns to moderate or low for 3 days.
The permittee shall be responsible for checking the fire index for the day of
the small slash burn using the website set forth in the permit.
   (B)   Burning of slash piles shall not be conducted within 50 feet of any
structure or combustible material. Conditions that could cause the fire to
spread shall be eliminated prior to ignition.
   (C)   Burning of slash piles shall not be left unattended while there is a
visible flame. The slash piles shall be monitored until all embers are
completely extinguished and cold.
   (D)   A minimum of one portable fire extinguisher with a minimum 4-A rating
or other approved on-site fire-extinguishing equipment, such as dirt, sand,
water-barrel, garden hose or water truck shall be available for immediate
utilization.
   (E)   Burning of rubbish or garbage is strictly prohibited.
(Ord. passed 11-15-2023)
§ 95.99 PENALTY.
   A violation of this chapter subject the person who violates any provision of
the chapter to a fine of $500 for each day of violation, in addition, any
person who violates this section is liable for civil damages for all injuries
caused by the fire.
(Ord. passed 11-15-2023)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 110.01 BUSINESS LICENSES REQUIRED.
   (A)   License. No business required to have a state sales tax license not
specifically exempt from municipal licensing shall engage in business without
first obtaining a business license through the Board of Trustees of the Town of
Keystone.
   (B)   Business defined. For purposes of this section, the term BUSINESS
shall include all and any activity engaged in by any person or entity, or
caused to be engaged in by any person or entity with the object of gain,
benefit or advantage, either direct or indirect.
      (1)   A separate business license shall be applied for and required if a
person or entity operates more than 1 business from the same location.
      (2)   A separate business license shall be required notwithstanding that
the person or entity operates more than 1 business under the same state sales
tax license.
      (3)   A person or entity who advertises or represents to the public that
more than 1 business is being operated from the same location, shall be
required to apply for and obtain separate business licenses for each respective
business.
(1992 Code, § 6-1-1) (Ord. 80-1991, passed 4-18-1990; Am. Ord. 80-1991, passed
9-18-1991; Am. Ord. 6-1-1.1, passed 10-19-2005) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-34-1
§ 110.02 APPLICATION FOR BUSINESS LICENSE.
   (A)   Applicant(s) for a business license shall fill out and file the
application form, as provided by the town in writing, with the town Finance
Officer.
   (B)   The application shall contain all information as required by the Board
of Trustees, Town of Keystone, and in certain cases, any information the County
Sheriff's Department may require the license for which application is made by
listing their state sales tax number.
(1992 Code, § 6-1-2) (Ord. 80-1991, passed 4-18-1990; Am. Ord. 80-1991, passed
9-18-1991)
§ 110.03 PROCEDURE FOR BUSINESS LICENSE APPLICATION.
   Unless otherwise provided, an application for a business license shall state
the following information:
   (A)   Name, address, date of birth and telephone number of applicant or
applicants;
   (B)   Trade name, if any, under which license is to be exercised;
   (C)   If partnership, the name, address, date of birth and telephone number
of each partner;
   (D)   If a corporation, the name, address, date of birth and telephone
numbers of the officers;
   (E)   Place of business or location where the license is to be exercised and
tax license number for the business;
   (F)   Description of the activity or nature of business to be carried on
under the license;
   (G)   The information as required by the Board of Trustees showing the
applicant is entitled to the license and that he or she is the proper person,
and the place a proper place for the exercise thereof;
   (H)   The information as required by ordinance as may be necessary for
determination of the amount of the license fee; and
   (I)   Furnish information in the case of security police, the owner of the
business must provide the local law enforcement with a list of all personnel
who will be carrying firearms within the town. This list must be up-dated
throughout the year as personnel are added or deleted from its employ.
(1992 Code, § 6-1-3) (Ord. 80-1991, passed 4-18-1990; Am. Ord. 80-1991, passed
9-18-1991)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see SDCL § 9-34-1

   Subject to ordinances establishing rules and regulations for buses,
licensing of animal drawn conveyances and business merchants, the fee for a
business license shall be determined by resolution of the Board of Trustees on

determined shall be paid during business hours at the Keystone Town Hall. Upon
receiving payment for the business license, the application shall be presented
to the Town Board for its approval. The monies as received shall be deposited
into the general fund.
(1992 Code, § 6-1-4) (Ord. 80A-1991, passed 3-2-1990; Am. Ord. 80-1990, passed
